THE PATTERN OF WHOLSO^^ WORDS.

Or a collection of such Truths as are of necessity to be believed unto
salvation, separated o^t of ^he body of all Theology

Made evident by infallible an^ plain proofs of Scripture.

And withal, The several uses such Principles should be put to, are
abundantly shevved.

A Project much desired, and of singular use for all sorts of Christians.

By N. Bifeild, Preacher of Gods Word at Isleworth in Middlesex.

2. TIM 1.13. Keep the true pattern of wholesome words, which, thou have heard
of me in faith and loue^ which is Christ Jesus.

AT LONDON, Imprinted by F. K. for Samuel Ma^^ dwelling in Paul's Church yard,
at the sign of the Swan. 1618.

To the most Noble Lady, the Lady DOROTHIE, Countess of Northumberland. And
to the highly honored Ladies her Daughters, The Lady DOROTHIE SYDNEY, and the
Lady LVCIE HAY: N. BYFEILD Wishes the abundance of true grace and peace.
Right Honorable,
I Have long since undertaken (as in the course of my Ministry you have often
heard) to extract out of al Theology contained in the Scriptures, the
Principles, that is, such doctrines which are fundamental, and absolutely
necessary to be known of as many as are to be saved. This Project ought to
be well accepted of all sorts of Christians, that wish their own good; partly
in respect of the necessity of the doctrines here collected under their
several heads; and partly in respect of the apparent evidence of the proofs of
Scripture, which are such, as make infallible demonstration to the conscience,
by the express light contained in them; and partly, because the Uses which may
be made of the several Principles, are every where abundantly showed.

And in as much as the Lord has been pleased, to give some testimony to my
endeavors herein in the public preaching; I am not out of hope, but that the
printing of those Principles may be profitable to many godly and plaine-hearted
Christians, that desire in the plainest manner to understand the meaning of
their heavenly Fathers will.

I humbly dedicate this work unto your Honors, and pray your acceptance, and
the patronage of it: and to give me leave in the view of the world to signify
this way, both my observance of the many noble and excellent virtues, which are
eminent in each of your Honors, as also my unfeigned thankfulness for the
many favors I have received, and for the countenance and encouragement of my
Ministry; accounting it a singular mercy of God, that any labors of mine
should find acceptance with persons of so high place and quality, or any way
be successeful to the prospering of any part of the work of Gods grace in your
hearts.

Now the God of all consolation, fill your Noble breasts with all riches of the
true grace that is in Jesus Christ; that you may abound in the knowledge of the
mysteries of his Kingdom in all judgment, and love of the truth which is
according to godliness, and in all those gifts which may be found unto honor,
and praise, and glory in the revelation of Jesus Christ.

Your Honors in all service N. Bifeild.
Isleworth, March 27. 1618.

FINIS.
CHAP. I. Containing the nature and use of this Treatise.
THe purpose and drift of this Treatise is to effect three things:

First to extract Theology contained in the Scriptures such truths, Things
intended in this Treatise.
as are of necessity to be believed unto salvation; the knowledge whereof is
required of all: In the defense whereof we should be ready to suffer the
extremest things, even death it self; and which we should account the very
Characters of true Religion, the distinct knowledge whereof we should lay up,
as great riches.





The benefit of attending to this course.
Singularly great would the profit of this project be, if there were a heart in
man to use a little diligence in matters of so great moment. Is it not a
marvelous benefit in this contending world for a man to know distinctly, what
truths be infallible; and to have the truths, that are absolutely necessary
to be believed, separated from such, as a man may be ignorant of, and yet be
saved?

And for the second thing, it is certain, the most Christians know their
grounds but by hearsay, and the common judgment of others: whereas here
they may be informed of them so, as to know them by proofs of Scripture,
which with a little labor they may commit to memory, as seed-plots of
contemplation.

And for the third, what is the reason, that Commonplace Divinity is so out
of use in popular teaching? or that Catechismes are looked upon so dully, and
learned or taught with so little profit? but that the use of such doctrine has
not been distinctly showed: so as men think of Principles, as of certain
inferior truths, because they see other points in textuall course handled with
directions for the use of them. Whereas it is certain, that no doctrines in
Religion have more abundant use in the life of man, nor more urged with
variety of uses in the Scriptures, then the heads of Catechism.

The warrant of this course.
And for the warrant of the project, it is evident, that the Apostles did make a
separation of truths, and did extract the fundamental truths out of the
maine body of doctrine, and those they delivered to ye Churches, as the common
treasure of all the Saints: and those both for the honor and use of them they
described by diverse titles.

They were called the principles of the praises of God, Heb. 5.12.

The principles of the doctrine of Christ, Heb. 6.1.

The doctrines of foundation in the same place.

The pattern of wholesome words, 2. Tim. 1.13.

The form of the knowledge of the truth, Romans 2.20.

The form of doctrine, into which they were delivered, Romans 6. All which
titles show the singular use of them.

Now if any ask me, Question.
how I will know a Principle?

I answer by these marks. Answer.


First, it is such a truth to be believed, Principles may be known three
ways.
as is contained in the express words of Scripture: so as I take a Principle
to be a Doctrine plainly expressed in the Word: and so differ from Doctrines,
that are deduced from the Scriptures only by consequence, or are there but in
dark and obscure words.

Secondly Principles are first truths, that is such, as have been from the
beginning, and have been believed in all ages of the Church.

Thirdly, they are such truths, as being stubbornely and wilfully denied, the
whole building falls down, and men hold not the foundation. Besides, any man
may be guided herein, that will make use of the judgment of the Churches in
their Creedes and Confessions, and Catechismes; though it be true, that if men
narrowly observe the most Catechismes, they either have not all Principles in,
or else they have more then Principles, such truths, as are strong meat, and
so prove hard sayings to the weak. Neither am I so transported with any
ouerweaning of my self in this project, but that with all readiness I shall
subject my endeavors herein to the correction of the godly learned: if my labor
may provoke others more sufficient to perfect this work with such exactnes, as
is further requisite, I shall rejoice in it, and think I have attained a happy
end.

I doubt not, but that this labor may be of great use for younger Divines to
point out a way, how they may Catechize with more profit by making the uses of
every Principle, as they teach the grounds to the people: yea, it is one part
of the Sabbaths days best employment in Sermons to treat in this, or the like
manner; and so to let the people be truly informed concerning the
Characteristicall truths in their Religion, with use of them in their
conversation.

Lastly, it will be some content unto ingenious minds, to see the Principles
cast into some method for the help of memory and quickening of delight, and
the more easy learning of them.

CHAP. II. The Method of the Principles.
The division of Principles according to their chief heads.
THe Principles concern either the fountain and original of Doctrine and
knowledge, which is the scripture or word of God; or the subject of knowledge,
which is God himself:

In God we consider: 1. His Nature: 2. His Works.

The works of God, as the principles take notice of them, are: 1. Creation: 2.
Providence:

The providence of God must be considered either in general, or as it
concerns man only.

The providence of God, as it concerns man has Principles, that look upon
him in his fourfold estate.

In the estate of Innocence.

In the estate of Corruption, or

In the estate of Grace, where 1 The means of grace, viz. Election in God; and
Redemption in Christ. 2 The subject of Grace, viz. the Church. 3 The degrees,
or sorts of Grace: viz. Justification, and Sanctification.


In the estate of Glory, where 1 Of the resurrection of the dead. 2 Of the last
judgment. 3 Of the glory of Heaven.


CHAP. III. Of the Scriptures.
2. Tim. 3.16. For the whole Scripture is given by inspiration of God, etc.


THe original or fountain of knowledge is the Scripture, that is, the books
of the old and new Testament, and those books were first called Scripture, Two
principles about the Scriptures.
in the new Testament.

There are two principles concerning the Scripture.



of themselves alone, to guide us in all things needful to salvation, without
adding ought to them, or diminishing ought from them.

For the first, that they are by divine inspiration, is infallibly evident from
the testimony of the Scriptures themselves, such as these. 2. Tim. 3.16. before
recited.

2. Pet. 1.20.21. So that ye first know this, that no prophecy of the
Scriptures is of any private interpretation. For the prophecy came not in old
time by the will of man: but holy men of God spoke as they were moved by the
holy Ghost.

And for our more abundant satisfaction, The Scripturs are the very word of
God, proved by testimonies external and internal.
there are other testimonies, that prove the Scriptures to be the very word
of God, and these both external and internal.

The external testimonies are such as these:

Moses the writer of the Law, and God testified his presence also by the cloud
and smoke about the Arc, in the Tabernacle, and Temple: Fire from heaven
devoured the sacrifices, and God gave answer by the Vrim and Thummim.





contained in the Scriptures.

The conversion of the souls Scriptures, and the comfort the godly find in
them in all afflictions.

The miraculous calling of the Moses and the Apostles, that wrote the
Scriptures, etc.

The internal testimony is the witness of Gods spirit, who in the hearts of
the godly does avouch so much, and this is a testimony proper to the household
of God.

Thus of the first principle.

The second Principle is, that the scriptures are perfect, which these places
show:

2. Tim. 3.17. That the man of God may be absolute, being made perfect unto
all good works.

Psalm. 19.7. The Law of the Lord is perfect, converting the soul: the
testimony of the Lord is sure, and gives wisdom unto the simple.

Gal. 1.8. But though that we, or an Angel from heaven preach unto you
otherwise, then that which we have preached unto you, let him be accursed.

John 1.7. Prou. 30.6. Revel. 22.18.
Duet. 12.32. Therefore whatsoever I command you, take heed you do it: thou
shall put nothing thereto, nor take ought therefrom.

Prou. 8.7.8. For my mouth shall speak the truth, and my lips abhor
wickedness.

All the words of my mouth are righteous and there is no leaudnes, nor
frowardness in them.

The uses.
The consideration of which principles may serve us for diverse uses; both for
instruction and reproof: for trial and for consolation: First, 1. For
instruction.
we should here be persuaded

To study the Scriptures with

John 5.39. Search the Scriptures: for in them you think to have eternal
life, and they are they, which testify of me.

Col. 3.16. Let the word of God, or Christ dwell in you plenteously in all
wisdom, teaching and admonishing your own selves, etc.

Psalm. 1.2. But his delight is in the Law of the Lord, and in his law does he
meditate day and night.

Laboring by all means to acquaint our children, and family with them.

Deuteronomy. 6.7. And thou shall rehearse them continually unto thy children, and
shall talk of them, when thou tariest in thy house, and as thou walk by the
way, and when thou lie down, and when thou risest up, etc.

For whatsoever things are written before time, are written for our learning,
that we through patience, and comfort of the scriptures, might have hope. They
are a sure word; we may rest upon them, 2. Pet. 1.20. as believing, that every
word of God is pure, and that God will make them good to such as trust in them,
Prou. 30.5.6.

Scriptures with all due preparation and attention, and high estimation,
receiving them as the word of God, and not of man: 1. These. 2.13. laboring to
bring clean hearts, and a meek and teachable spirit to them, as being able to
save our souls: James 1.21.22. with a resolution to do whatsoever God
requires in them.

We should love them above

We should therefore make whether our works be wrought in God, and showing
the power of the word in the demonstration of the apparent life of it, in
commanding all our particular actions, that men may see the light of the word
in the light of our good works.

Phil. 2.15. That we may be blameless and pure, and the sons of God,
without rebuke in the midst of a naughty and crooked nation, amongst whom you
shine as lights in the world.

Gal. 6.16. And as many as walk according to this rule, peace shall be upon
them, and mercy upon the Israel of God.

Psalm. 119.105. Thy word is a lantern unto my feet, and a light unto my path.

Yea we should daily try and search the secrets of our hearts by it, as that
which only can do it. Heb. 4.12. For the word of God is lively, and mighty in
operation, and sharper then any two edged sword, and enters through even unto
the dividing asunder of the soul and the spirit, and of the joints and the
marrow, and is a discerner of the thoughts and intents of the heart.

We should therefore in all think of no man, above what is written, Gal. 1.7.
1. Cor. 4.6. Esaias 8.20.

Thus much for instruction.

Secondly, For reproof.
these Principles reprove the Papists and carnal Protestants, and the godly
too:

The Papists are here reproved, Of the Papists in 4. things.


1. For making the authority of the Scriptures to depend upon the testimony of
the Church, whereas the Church is built upon the Scriptures, Ephesians. 2.20. And
are built upon the foundation of the Apostles and Prophets; Jesus Christ
himself being the chief corner stone.

2. For not holding it to be sufficient without traditions, contrary to the
express word, 2. Tim. 3.17. That the man of God may be absolute, being made
perfect unto all good works.

3. For withholding the Scriptures from the common people, keeping from them
the sight of their Fathers will, contrary to the word, John 5.39. Search the
Scriptures: for in them you think to have eternal life, and they are they
which testify of me.

Col. 3.16. Let the word of God dwell in you plenteously in all wisdom, etc.

4. For judging controversies without them: contrary to the commandment, Esaias
8.20. To the Law, and to the Testimony. If they speak not according to this
word, it is because there is no light in them.

The carnal Protestants are here

1. For their miserable neglect of the reading, Of Carnal Protestants.
hearing, meditation, and the care to yield obedience to the Scriptures: yea,
for the wretched neglect of the very buying of the Bible for their use, and the
use of their families, and for daring to live without the preaching of the word
in times of spiritual famine.

2. For their vilde audaciousnesse, that dare live in such sins, as they hear
threatened in the Scriptures, profanely despising the warning daily given them,
Esaias 30.11.12. Ier. 23.9.10.

3. For their scorning and deriding of such, as honor the word, and frequent
the hearing of it.

Esaias 57.3.4. But you witches children come hither, the seed of the adulterer,
and of the whore: On who^ have you iested? Upon whom have you gaped, and thrust
out your tongs? Are ye not rebellious children, and a false seed?

4. For their irreuerence, when they come to the house of God to hear, Eccles.
5.1.

Of the godly.
1. For their distractions in the hearing and reading of the Word. 2. For
neglecting the counsels and directions given out of the Word. 3. For not
resting upon it through unbelief. 4. For too much aptnes to receive opinions,
if they come from men they account godly, though they have no warrant from the
word. There be traditions on the right hand, as well as on the left.


Thus much for reproof.

Thirdly, For trial.
we may all try our selves, what we are by our respect of the Scriptures: If
we love and hear the word, we are of God, Ioh. 8.47. He that is of God,
hears Gods word: ye therefore hear them not, because ye are not of God. Gods
people are a people, in whose hearts is Gods Law, Esaias 51.7. Psalm. 37.31.

Lastly, For consolation.
it may be a singular consolation to all such, as find the word of God to
testify with the^: it matters not what the world says, or thinks of us; if we
can find that the word of the Lord is good concerning us: our hearts may be at
rest, when God speaks peace by his word, and we may be sure we are in the
right way, when we follow the directions of the word.

CHAP. IIII. Of God.
Psalm. 72.18.19.
HItherto of the principles concerning the fountain of knowledge: the subject
of knowledge is God, who must be considered two ways: first, In his nature:
secondly; In his works.

Principles concerning God.
Concerning God considered in his nature, there are four principles:

that there is a God.

glorious in Nature.

three in Persons.

one in Essence.

every leaf, yea almost in every line of Scripture; and therefore I spare
quotations, it being out of all doubt, that the Scripture says so.

And against all seeds of Atheism, That there is a God, is proved, first by
testimonies internal.
men may keep in their minds these other testimonies; both inward and outward.

The inward testimonies that prove there is a God, are these:

The horror of conscience, that sin, dreading a supreme Judge; which
terrors we see are oftentimes such, as are most dreadful, and such as no
outward thing can still.

The testimony of the holy Ghost infallibly satisfying the godly herein.

The revelation of God to the which presence of God they likewise miss, if
they sin presumptuously.

By testimonies external, and so either in the world,
The external testimonies are taken from the works of God; either more
generally in the world; or more specially in the Church.

The world testifies there is a God;





Judgments that fall upon the wicked, sometimes in the very act of sinning, and
sometimes at the very instant of the wishes of wicked persons.

times acknowledged a God.

In the Church God has proved himself to be: or in the Church.
1 By apparitions: God has showed himself by certain forms, or signs of
his presence: thus Adam, Noah, Abraham, Isaac, Jacob, Moses, etc. saw God. 2 By
the miracles wrought beyond all the course of nature: as when he raised dead
men; divided the sea; made the Sun go backward, etc.


Thus of the proof of the first principle.

That God is also maruellously

Exodus 33.18. Again, he said, I beseech thee show me thy glory.

19. And he answered, etc.

Esa. 6.2.3. And one cried to another, and said, Holy, holy, holy is the Lord
of hosts: the whole world is full of his glory.

1. Tim. 6.16. Who only has immortality, and dwells in the light that none
can attain unto, whom never man saw, neither can see, unto whom be honor,
and power everlasting, Amen.

Glories in the nature of God.
And how can he be but exceeding glorious, when as he is,

Incorporeall, beyond the perfection God is a spirit.

Before the mountains were made, and before thou had formed the earth, and
the world, even from everlasting to everlasting thou art our God.

Is it true indeed that God will dwell on the earth? Behold the heavens, and
the heavens of heavens are not able to contain thee, how much more unable is
this house that I have built.

Ier. 23.24. Do not I fill heaven and earth, says the Lord?

Immutable without shadow Every good giving, and every perfect gift is from
above, and comes down from the father of lights, with whom is no
variableness, neither shadow by turning.

Finally, we should strive to get and increase in the true knowledge of our

rules.
we should study his glory; but then we must be warned, when we go about this
study, to look to diverse things.

1. We must repent us of our sins, for this knowledge requires a clean heart.

2. We must bring an humble and teachable mind: Psalm. 25.9. Them that be
meek will he guide in judgment, and teach the humble his way.

3. Let the Word be thy guide: look for him in the Word: Thou must captiuate
thy Reason, and advance thy faith.

4. Thou must go to the Son to reveal the Father: pray Christ to show thee
the Father: Ioh. 1.18, No man has seen God at any time: the only begotten
Son, which is in the bosom of the Father; he has declared him, etc.

5. Pray for the spirit of revelation to form this in thee, and resolve to get
thy heart established in the knowledge of God, by many prayers.

6. Observe him in his Image in his children, get affection to them, and live

God is love.

No man has seen God at any time; if we love one another, God dwells in

For Information: The glory Lord shall endure for ever: For information.

For Instruction, and so the Uses for instruction.


1. To fear him, and stand in awe of him, even all the inhabitants of the
earth, who are the work of his hands, Psalm. 33.6.7.8.

2. To study the knowledge of these works of his; to remember them,
contemplate of them, and praise his workmanship, and admire his glory, that
does great things, and unsearchable, yea marvelous things without number, etc,
Job 9.10.11. shall we not sing unto the Lord all our life, and praise our God
while we live, etc, Psalm. 104 33. seeing The heavens declare the glory of God,
and the firmament shows the work of his hands, Psalm. 19.1. and the invisible
things of him, that is, his eternal power and Godhead are seen by the
creation of the World, being considered in his works, etc, Romans 1.20. Let us
remember, that God gave a Sabbath, of purpose to remember the glory of God in
the creation.

3. To observe the distinct glory of every person, admire that Son, by whom
God made the worlds, Heb. 1.3. Col. 1.16. and that Spirit, that sitting upon
that Chaos, first hatched it, Genes. 1.2.

4. To acknowledge Gods sovereignty, let him take whom he will away, who can
say, what do thou, Job 9.13. God will not withdraw his anger, and the most
mighty helps stoop under him.

5. Upon all occasions, and in all distresses to seek unto him for help,
assistance and succor: Psalm. 124.8. Psalm. 134.3. yea believing in him,
though we see no hope in respect of outward means, Rom 4.17. Heb. 11.3. Isaiah
37.16.

And as this is true of affliction, and outward distresses; so is it true of
all spiritual distresses about the means or matter of holiness: for God
himself uses the word (create) in both, to show us, that it is lawful for
that reason to rest upon him, Isaiah 57.19, I create the fruit of the lips to
be peace, etc. Psalm. 51.10. Create in me a clean heart, etc. so it is applied
to good works, Ephesians. 1.10. and to our protection in general, Esaias 4.4. and 5.
To show, that if it were as difficult, as to make heaven and earth at the
first, yet God will do it.

6. To teach us compassion to the creatures, we should love the work of his
hands, and not be cruel to them, or void of pity.

Uses for reproof.

perpetual, that it cannot pass it, etc.

and wine are in their feasts: but they regard not the work of the Lord,

For information: this is a glorious For information.
and if we search into it distinctly, there are many things admirable in Gods
government; Things admirable in Gods providence.
as,

1 First, ye vicegerency of Christ his Son, Heb. 1.3. Who being the brightness
of the glory, and the engraued form of his person, and bearing up al things by
his mighty word, etc.

2 Secondly, the splendour of the means he uses, even Kings on earth are his
servants, Pro. 21.1. The Kings heart is in the hand of the Lord, as the rivers
of waters: he turns it whithersoeuer it pleases him: yea Angels in heaven,
Oh the admirable glory of the government of angels in the world! as is shadowed
out in Ezech. 1.4. to 15.

3 The variety of means he has, and can raise; even all the armies in heaven
and earth.

4 His working sometimes without means, Genes. 2.

5 His working against means sometimes, Psalm. 105.12. to 16. The Sun must
stand still: Fire must not burn: the Sea must not drown, etc.

6 The extent of his government; what a work to order all things?

7 The preservation of all the sorts of things even by the word of God: By
succession perpetuating his creation; and supporting all things, providing
daily for them.

8 The destruction he makes amongst the creatures, Psa. 104.29. By deluge,
fire, sword, pestilence, tumbling down Monarchies, etc, Psalm. 68.1.

9 The ordering of the disorders of the world, turning sin to good, as an
Apothecary does poison; and directing evil instruments, wicked men, to punish
the wicked, or to correct the godly. To see how God looks one way, and they
another. Nabuchadnezzar intends to satisfy his own pride, revenge, ambition,
covetousness: yet God guides it to another use, even to correct his people,
which he shows by burning his rod, Esa. 10.5.6. Esa. 14.5.6. and 29. and God
directs the evil actions of the wicked to a good end: so of the Jews in
killing Christ, etc.

10 But especially his admirable disposing of all things, notwithstanding the
infinite multitude of all things in the world, which is shadowed in the
wheels, Ezech. 1.15. etc.

11 All this to be done without labor, or vexation: say therefore, as Psalm.
104.1.24. My soul praise thou the Lord: O Lord my God, thou art exceeding
great, thou art clothed with glory and honor.

O Lord how manifold are thy works! in wisdom have thou made them all: the
earth is full of thy riches.

his praise?

CHAP. VII. Of Man's first estate, viz. of Innocence.
Eccles. 7.31. Only lo, this have I found, that God has made man righteous:
but they have sought many inventions.


THere are two principles concerning man's first estate.

God made man at Furthermore God said, Let us make man in our own image
according to our likeness, and let them rule over the fish of the sea, etc.

1. Cor. 11.7. For a man ought not to cover his head, for as much as he is the
image of God, etc.

Colos. 3.10. And have put on the new man, which is renewed in knowledge after
the image of him that created him.

Only lo, this have I found, that God has made man righteous: but they have
sought many inventions.

Ephesians. 4.24. And put on the new man, which after God is created in
righteousness, and true holiness.

Note, that I say, chiefly (as that which is a principle): for else man was
created after the image of God:

Man was after the Image of God three ways.
either of the, 1. Being of God: or 2. Of the manner of his being. 1. Of his
being, as he has in him a spirit, a nature: 1. Spiritual incorporeall. 2.
Immortal. 3. Invisible. 4. Intelligible.
2. Of the manner of his being: for as in man is one soul, and yet diverse
faculties, as cogitation, memory, will, etc. so is there in God one essence,
and three persons.



Secondly, in respect of his eminency, Lord of all, Genes. 1.26. Furthermore
God said, Let us make man in our Image, according to our likeness, and let
them rule over the fish of the sea, and over the foul of the heaven, and over
the beasts, and over all the earth, and over every thing that creeps and
moves on the earth.

Psalm. 8.6.7.8. Thou have made him to have dominion in the works of thine
hands: thou have put all things under his feet, etc. For if the man be Gods
image for the Sovereignty, he has in the family, as 1. Cor. 11.7. and the
Maiestrate for his superiority in the Commonwealth, Psalm. 82. much more man in
general for dominion over all.

1. In respect of knowledge: for in the mind of man, there is hid,
a-resemblance of Gods wisdom to know God, his will, and works with the
natures and properties of them. 2. In respect of original Justice, which stood
in the rectitude of his nature, the spirit subject to God, the soul to the
spirit, the body to the soul without any sin. 3. In respect of freedom of
will.


There are four sorts of free-willes: 1. Only to good; so in good Angels, and
the blessed. 2. Only to evil; so in devils and the wicked. 3. Partly to
evil, and partly to good; so in the regenerate on earth. 4. So to good, as it
might be to evil; so in Adam, etc.


The power of his freedom was such, as he could do all things convenient to
his estate; whether,

Works of nature, as eat,

Works of policy; as govern

Or, Works religious: 1. Internal; to love, fear, and trust in God. 2.
External; to teach, pray, sacrifice, etc.


The uses follow.

The uses.
We should inform our The special favor of God to man in his Creation.
when he had provided all things made for him:

But in the place in Paradise,

And in the manner --

Both of making his body. He did not say, let it be; but as it were, framed
all with his own hands; the man of the dust, the woman of the rib:

And of inspiring his soul, he breathed the breath of lives into him,

Genes. 2.7. The Lord God made the man also of the dust of the ground, and
breathed in his face breath of life, and the man was a living soul.

He begat his soul as it were a divine spark or particle of God; therefore
called the Father of spirits, Heb. 12.9. Zach. 12 1. Acts 17.28.

And in both he says, let us make; calling all the Trinity to the care and
workmanship.

But especially that he should as it were, be made like unto God himself; and
therefore let us sing, as Psalm. 8.3, What is man that thou thus mindest him,
etc.

Of true blessedness, wherein viz. not in idleness, riches, lust, pleasure,
sports, etc. for none of all this was in paradise, yet Adam happy perfectly,
etc.

The second use is for instruction,

Duties.
1. Unto God; To God.
and so first we should with all thankfulness affectionately acknowledge his
love to man.

2. It should instruct man earnestly to study and endeavor, To know God, To
fear, To resemble him. To praise his workmanship.


For these were the ends of man's creation, no other creatures could reach it;
therefore God made man reasonable. We do not answer the end of our creation,
if we make not God in some sort visible by our holiness, and praise his works,
etc.

To our selves.
and so it should teach us:

1. First, to care for the precious and immortal soul, yt God has breathed
into us above all, as Matthew. 16.26. For what shall it profit a man, though he
should win the whole world, if he lose his own soul? or what shall a man give
for the recompense of his soul? What should we dote on temporal things, when
our souls are created to the possession of eternal blessedness?

2. To be patient, and trust upon God in distress, Psalm. 22.11. Be not far
from me, because trouble is near; for there is none to help me, etc.

Psalm. 139.14. I will praise thee, for I am fearfully and wondrously made:
marvelous are thy works, and my soul knows it well.

3. To lament our fall.

4. To study our recovery, and we see hence what to seek, viz. knowledge and
goodness.

5. To long for the time mentioned, Psalm. 17.15. When we shall be satisfied
with his Image.

To other men.


1. First, wrong not man: for he is Gods image, Genes. 9.6. Who so sheadeth
man's blood, by man shall his blood be shed: for in the image of God has he
made man.

2. Love one another, especially where this Image is repaired: for we were
created to this end, that we should delight one in another.



1. For our insensiblenesse, forgetfulness, and vncapablenesse of these
considerations, especially for our want of lamentation for the ruins in our
nature.

2. For our horrible neglect of knowledge and goodness, without which man is
more like a beast; yea, in respect of sin like a Devil.

3. Of the Papists about pictures Image.

CHAP. VIII. Of the fall of Man.
Eccles. 7.29. Only lo, this have I found, that God has made man righteous:
but they have sought many inventions.


THe misery of man in his estate of corruption must be considered two ways:

In the cause of it.

In the parts of it.

The cause of it was the fall of our first parents, concerning which are these
principles:

Adam and Eve fell, Principles concerning the fall of man.
and lost speedily the happiness, in which they were created, as appears,
Genes. 3.7. etc. and thus they did loose God; Paradise: Gods Image.


And that they lost it speedily appears, in that the devil is called a
murderer from the beginning, and the fall is presently related after the story
of his innocence in the creation.

Wherefore as by one man sin entered into the world, and death by sin: and
so death went over all men, for as much as all men have sinned.

Eccles. 7.29. as before.

defiled, and deprived of the glory of God, Romans 5.12. as before. 18.19.
Likewise then as by the offense of one, the fault came on all men to
condemnation; so by the righteousness of one, the benefit abounded toward all
men to the justification of life.

For as by one man's disobedience many were made sinners: so by the obedience of
one shall many also be made righteous.

The uses follow.

The uses of these woeful principles may be first for information, and so we
should study to satisfy, and settle our hearts more at large concerning two
things.

The one is the grieuousnes of

The other is the Justice of God

For the first, there be many things may assure us, that the sin of our first
parents was a most grievous sin: for it admits fearful aggrauations; as,
Things to show the greatness of Adams sin.
1. That they durst venture all their happiness about so small an advantage to
them. If we think, it was a small offense to eat an apple; think with all, it
was a desperate wickedness to venture eternal life for the possession of an
apple. 2. This was Gods first commandment that he gave them, and to neglect
God so soon in a thing, wherein they might so easily have obeyed, must needs
appear to be desperate wickedness. 3. This sin was committed, when they had no
inward concupiscence to tempt them, nor that pronenesse of nature, that is in
man now to sin. 4. They offended, when God had abundantly provided for them;
they wanted nothing that was good for them. 5. They herein violated the whole
Law, because they broke the agreeme^ts which were made between God and them:
according to that of James 2.10, For whosoever shall keep the whole Law, and
yet fails in one point, he is guilty of all. 6. Because it was a sacramental
fruit: to cast bread to dogs is no great offense; but to cast consecrated bread
to dogs is a grievous sin. 7. This sin was accompanied with diverse
monstrous sins; first, horrible doubting of Gods truth: secondly, compacting
with Gods utter enemy, and so making Apostasy from God to the Devil: thirdly,
consent to the blasphemies of the devil, when he spoke enuiously, and
scoffingly at God: fourthly, affectation of divinity: fifthly, a wretchlesse
disregard of what should become of his posterity, through his ventrous course:
with many other sins.


Adam was the common root of all mankind, and we were in his loins, as Leui
was in Abraham's, when he paid tithes; and are not traitors punished in their
children? the Act of a burgess in the Parliament is the Act of the country.

Object.
But yet at least godly men should not beget ungodly children.

Answ.
They beget children, as men, not as godly men; I mean, they derive such a
nature as they have, which is corrupt after calling: though they be justified
perfectly, yet they are sanctified but in part: The father that was
circumcised, did beget a child that was uncircumcised; and take the cleanest
corn in the world, and sow it, and it brings forth chafe in the ear with the
corn.

Thus much for information.

The doctrine of the fall may serve also for instruction; and so both in
general. particular.


In general it should teach us four things:

First, to take heed of the fountains Apostacy. There were three things
occasioned mightily the fall of our first parents:

The first was a rebellious desire to be, Occasions of Apostasy.
what God would not have us to be.

The second unthankfulness: all the pleasures of Paradise will not please
them, if they be crossed in some one thing, though never so little.

The liberty they took to add or detract from Gods word: they added the word
touch, and they detracted, when they said, lest ye die: and these three sins
are, and ever will be, causes of Apostacy; if they be not prevented.

Apostates are like the devil; they will not be quiet, till they make others
fall away with them.

of lesser sins: we see here what the eating of an apple did, which the most
men would feign think was but a small matter; and the rather, because
monstrous sins may be committed about a small offense in it self. Think of
the man that gathered sticks on the Sabbath day, and of the case of Ananias
and Sapphira.

We must get on our armor, Devil. We see here how he thirsts after the ruin
of man; and if he prevailed so over Adam, how much more easily may he prevail
over us? and if he could deceive by the means of a serpent there; how much
more now, when he speaks to us by men like our selves? yea then we saw a
proof of it, For how quickly was Adam enticed, when the devil spoke to him in
the mouth of Eve his wife.

And we may here observe the Devils method in tempting, and the degrees of
tentation: For there was Degrees of the devils tentation.
1. First, the suggestion it self. 2. The obscuring of the thoughts about the
eminency of God, and the excellency of the image received of him. 3. An
impression of forgetfulness in the memory, not distinctly remembering what was
before done, or commanded of God. 4. The tickling of ambition, affecting to be
more then they were. 5. Trust given to the flatteries and baits of the devil,
and a contracted familiarity with him, with inclination of the will and
affection to the prohibited fruit.


Thus much in general.

In particular, four sorts must be warned: 1. First, women should here be
much humbled, and for ever be mistrustfull of their Counsels, and carriage: for
Satan knows how to make use of them still. 2. Secondly, men must take heed of
the whisperings, and enticing advice of women. 3. Thirdly, the weak must
carefully look to themselves, that Satan employ not them as instruments of
tentations; and they should learn not to be so violent in things they are not
fully grounded in. 4. The strong must take heed lest they fall: If Adam fell in
Paradise, they are in more danger now in the world; neither may they trust in
their own gifts, but learn to place all their trust in God. 5. As any are
more godly, so they must know they shall be more assaulted.


Thus for instruction.

This doctrine of the fall has matter in it of extreme humiliation, in that
eternal shame lies upon our nature by this vile offense, both in respect of
the extremity of our loss, and the fearful displeasure of God.

Lastly, it may comfort the godly to think of their estate by Christ, having
received the assurance of a better condition, then ever they could have had in
Adam; and the rather, because they are now confirmed as the Angels of heaven,
that they can never fall from the happiness they have in Christ.

CHAP. IX. Of Sin.
Romans 5.12. Wherefore, as by one man sin entered into the world, and death by
sin; and so death went over all men; for as much as all men have sinned, etc.


HItherto of the cause of our misery.

The parts follow, viz. 1. Sin. 2. Punishment.


The principles concerning sin, Principles concerning sin.
are,

First, that all men have sinned, The fool has said in his heart, there is no
God: they have corrupted and done an abominable work; there is none that does
good.

The Lord looked down from heaven upon the children of men, to see if there
were any that would understand and seek God.

All are gone out of the way, they are all corrupt, there is none that does
good, no not one.

Prou. 20.9. Who can say I have made mine heart clean? I am clean from my
sin?

1. King. 8.46. There is no man that sins not, etc.

Eccles. 7.22. Surely there is no man just in the earth, that does good, and
sins not.

Romans 3.9. What then, are we more excellent? No in no wise: for we have
already proved, that all both Jews and Gentiles are under sin.

Iam. 3.2. For in many things we sin all.

1. Ioh. 1.8. If we say that we have no sin, we deceive our selves, and the
truth is not in us.

The second principle is, that Who can bring a clean thing out of filthiness?
there is not one.

Job 15.14. What is man that he should be clean? and he that is born of a
woman that he should be just?

Psalm. 51.5. Behold I was borne in iniquity, and in sin has my mother
conceived me.

That this infection has ouerspread the whole nature of man, principle: we
must consider that the nature of man is tainted 14. ways: For there is in man
by nature,

Extreme darkness, Foul blemishes in every man's nature.
sightlesnes, especially in the knowledge of God and happiness.

Colos. 1.13. Who has delivered us from the power of darkness.

1. Cor. 2.14. But the natural man perceives not the things of the spirit of
God, for they are foolishness unto him; neither can he know them, because
they are spiritually discerned.

Having their cogitation darkened, and being strangers from the life of God,
through the ignorance that is in them, because of the hardness of their heart,
etc.

He feeds of ashes; a seduced heart has deceived him, that he cannot deliver
his soul, nor say, is there not a lie in my right hand?



Romans 8.7. For the wisdom of the flesh is enmity to God.

Romans 7.23. But I see another law in my members, rebelling against the law of
my mind, and leading me captive unto the law of sin, which is in my members.

5. Impurity, foulnes, filthiness, all over, Tit. 1^ 5. Unto them that are
defiled (...) ^^beleeuing, is nothing pure, (...) even their minds and
conscien^^ are defiled.

Psalm. 14.3. All are gone out of the way, they are all corrupt, there is none
that does good, no not one.

6. Abundance of false principles.

7. Pronenesse to al sorts of evil, Romans 7.14.21. For we know that the law is
spiritual, but I am carnal, sold under sin.

I find then by the law, that when I would do good, evil is present with me,
etc.

Concupiscence.

All are gone out of the way, they are all corrupt, there is none that does
good, no not one, etc.

Romans 3.10. As it is written, There is none righteous, no not one.

Neither give you your members as weapons of unrighteousness unto sin, etc.

Know ye not, that to whomsoever ye give your selves as servants to obey, his
servants you are to whom ye obey; whether it be of sin unto death, or of

Christ himself is an offense: a rock of offense, 1. Cor. 8.7. 1. Pet. 2.6.

A natural sauouring and relishing Satan, Ephesians. 2.2. Wherein in time past you
walked according to the course of this world, and after the prince that rules
in the air, even the spirit that now works in the children of disobedience?
This has been ever since the first tentation in Paradise.

Corruption of memory.

Forgetting Good. Retaining Evil.
A natural disunion one from From whence are wars and contentions amongst
you? are they not hence, even of your lusts that fight in your members.

These things prove that we have all vile natures, that there is not one of a
good nature in the world by nature.

principle is, that besides these sins that stick fast upon our natures,
every man is guilty of horrible, and many, and vile actual sins, Psalm. 14.
1.2.3. They have corrupted and done an abominable work, etc.

Job. 15.15.16. Behold he found no steadfastness in his Saints: yea the heavens
are not clean in his sight.

How much more is man abominable and filthy, who drinks iniquity like water.

Rom, 3.12. They have all gone out of the way, etc.

Such as are,

1. A world of evil thoughts, Genes. 6.5. When the Lord saw that the
wickedness of man was great in the earth, and all the imaginations of the
thoughts of his heart were only evil continually.

Atheistical thoughts, innumerable. Impure thoughts, innumerable. Vain
thoughts, innumerable.
Errors in all parts of Religion.

2. Vile affections: Impatiency: Lust: Anger: Envy: Suspicion: Malice: Worldly
fear: Trust: Joy: Love, etc.

3. Vile words: bitter, idle, false, flattering, sla^dering, proud, filthy,
deceitful, scornful, censuring words.

4. Atheistical works, Psalm. 14.1.3. as in many places before.

Against Gods worship in all the parts. Against the Sabbath. In our particular
and general calling. At home and abroad. Secret, open. Of omission, and
commission. Of ignorance, of knowledge. Sudden, and of custom. In company, out
of co^mpanie.
Hypocrisy, pride, security, unbelief, impenitency, etc.

In prosperity, adversity, etc.

Partaking with others sin.

Our own righteousness, as Esa. 64.6. is as filthy clouts, and we all do
fade like a leaf, and our iniquities like the wind have taken us away.

Besides personal faults, as drunkenness, usury, swearing, whoredom, etc.
works of the flesh, Galath. 5.19.20.21 Moreover the works of the flesh are
manifest, which are adultery, fornication, uncleanness, wantonness, etc.

The uses of these principles are fourefold. Uses for information.


First for information, and that

1. That there can be no justification by our works, Romans 9.20. Therefore by
the works of the law shall no flesh he justified in his sight; for by the law
comes the knowledge of sin.

Psalm. 130.3. If thou (O Lord) straightly markest iniquities, (O Lord) who shall
stand?

For every mouth must be stopped, and all the world be guilty before God.

2. That the cause of all Gods dis-regard of us, and the miseries that befall
us, is in our selves.

How can we murmr at our crosses, if we look upon our sins? There is
mercy in the greatest Judgment: for it is his mercy we are not consumed, Lam.
3.22. It is the Lords mercy that we are not consumed, because his compassions
fail not, etc.

If Adams one sin deserved it, what do all these in us.

3. That it will never go well with the wicked, though God forbear for a long
time, Eccles. 8.11.12. Because sentence against an evil work is not executed
speedily: therefore the heart of the children of men is fully set to do evil.

But it shall not be well to the wicked, neither shall he prolong his days;
he shall be like a shadow, because he fears not before God.

4. That no man has cause to brag of his good nature, there are so many
springs of sin, within us.

5. That the things that defile a man, are from within, in himself, it is not
any outward deformity, ill clothes, natural foulness, etc.

6. That a little repentance will not serve the turn.

7. That there is difference between the wicked, and the godly in sinning.

8. Concerning Gods providence in the death of Infants: we kill young snakes
and adders, because they will sting, as well as the old, because they have
stung.

9. Say not, God is the cause of our ruin: nor is it thy chance, or ill luck,
or only the devil, that brought thee into this or that mischief: it is thine
own ill nature.

Secondly, for humiliation:

First, to the godly in two respects: 1. Because they find so many of their old
corruptions, having received such graces and mercies from God: 2. Because they
yet are the means of the conueiance of original sin to their children.


Secondly, to such wicked men as live in open sins, yet repent not. Why does
their hearts carry them away? Job 15.12.14.

Have the workers of iniquity no knowledge? are they guilty of so many
reasons, and fallen into the hands of a righteous Judge, and yet secure? Psalm.
82.5. They know not and understand nothing, they walk in darkness, albeit
all the foundations of the earth be moved.

Things make civil honest men miserable.
how vild their estate is, though God have restrained some evils in them: for
1. They want the Image of God. 2. They have an infected nature in all the
former fourteen things. 3. There is in them a disabilitie in the manner of all
holy duties. 4. They partake of other men's sins many ways. 5. They are
guilty of many omissions. 6. They abound in inward sins, by which God is
vexed, as Genes. 6.5. When the Lord saw that the wickedness of man was great
in the earth, and all the imaginations of the thoughts of his heart were only
evil continually: and Satan by the^ can set vp^^ strong holds, 2, Co. 10.5. 7.
They are guilty of many outward evils against the least commandments.


The third use is for instruction, and so strong Christians should learn to
admire and praise God

1. That could be pacified: Oh what is man, that God should here look upon
such a dounghill!

2. That has so vouchsafed to make us clean in part from such filthiness,
taking away the body of sins, and seasoning the fountain, and drying it up.

Christians should never be at rest, till they get assurance of their pardon
in the blood of Jesus Christ.



1. Sold strive after the contrary holiness, and to express the reformation
of their natures and lives, Ephesians. 4.22. and cast off concerning the
conversation in times past, the old man, which is corrupt through the
deceivable lusts* etc.

2. Should walk humbly all their days, because of the many remainders of
corruption, as Romans 7.15.16. etc. For I allow not that which I do: for what I
would, that do I not: but what I hate, that do I. and look to their hearts,
Heb. 3.12. Taking heed lest at any time there be in any of them an evil heart,
and unfaithful to depart away from the living God. And looking to it, that sin
reign no more, Romans 6.16. etc.

3. It should work in all the godly a wonderful desire of final redemption,
Romans 7.24. O wretched man that I am, who shall deliver me from the body of this
death! Psalm. 14.7. Oh give salvation unto Israel out of Zion, when the Lord
turns the captivity of his people, then Jacob shall rejoice, and Israel shall
be glad.

Oh how should we desire to get out of the world! seeing all so leprous, the
plague sore running upon every man, so as we are in danger to be infected in
all places, and by all persons.

4. It should work in wicked men a fervent desire of remission, and constant
endeavor in the confession of sin, crying out daily with the leper, unclean,
unclean.



1. First, to all men for the Lord uses this, as an argument of pity and
mercy, Genes. 8.21. And the Lord smelled a savor of rest, and the Lord said in
his heart, I will hence forth curse the ground no more for man's cause: for the
imaginations of man's heart is evil even from his youth, neither will I smite
any more all things living, as I have done. Isaiah 48.8.9. I knew that thou
would grievously transgress; therefore have I called thee a transgressor
from thy womb: yet for my name sake will I defer, etc. 2. Chro. 6.35.36.
Then hear thou in heaven their prayer, and their supplication, and judge their
cause:

If they sin against thee (for there is no man that sins not), and thou be
angry with them, and deliver them unto the enemies, and they take them, and
carry them away captive unto a land far and near, etc.

2. To the godly: they should admiringly rejoice in their privilege in the
blood of Christ, and in the remission of all their sins.

CHAP. X. Of the punishment of sin.
Romans 5.12. Wherefore as by one man sin entered into the world, and death by
sin: and so death went over all men, for as much as all men have sinned.


HItherto of the principles concerning sin: Now concerning the punishment of
sin, follows this principle, viz.

That all men in their natural estate are extremely miserable, in respect of
the punishment, unto which they are liable for their sins.

Nahum. 1.2.3.6. God is ielous, and the Lord reuengeth, even the Lord of anger,
the Lord will take vengeance on his adversaries, and he reserueth wrath for his
enemies.

The Lord is slow to anger: but he is great in power, and will not surely
clear the wicked: the Lord has his way in the whirlewind, and in the storm,
and the clouds are the dust of his feet.

Who can stand before his wrath, or who can abide in the fiercenes of his
wrath? his wrath is poured out like fire, and the rocks are broken by him, etc.

Romans 5.12. Job 10.17. Thou renewest thy plagues against me, and thou
increasest thy wrath against me: changes and armies of sorrows are against me.

Job. 31.3. Is not destruction to the wicked, and strange punishments to the
workers of iniquity?

2. These. 1.9. Which shall be punished with everlasting perdition from the
presence of the Lord, and from the glory of his power.

Ephesians. 2.3. Among whom we also had our conversation in times past in the lusts
of our flesh, in fulfilling the will of the flesh and of the mind, and wear by
nature the children of wrath, as well as others.

That this principle may be explicated, I will reckon up the several sorts of
punishments, which have been inflicted for man's sin.

17. sorts of punishments inflicted on man for his sin.
1. The loss of Paradise, from which we are all exiled, so as we live as
banished men, while we are in this world, Genes. 3.24. Thus he cast out man,
and at the East side of the Garden of Eden he set the Cherubines, and the
blade of a sword shaken, to keep the way of the tree of life.

2. The curse of the creatures: the creatures are subject to vanity, and
subdued unto bondage, under which they groan for man's sin, Romans 8.20.21.
Because the creature is subject to vanity, not of it own will, but by reason
of him which has subdued it under hope, etc. the earth was cursed for our
sakes, Genes. 3.17.18. Cursed is the earth for thy sake, in sorrow shall thou
eat of it all the days of thy life.

Thorns also and thistles shall it bring forth unto thee, and thou shall eat
the herb of the field.

3. An impure and painful birth, Genes. 3.16. Unto the woman he said, I will
greatly increase thy sorrows, and thy conceptions: in sorrow shall thou bring
forth children; and thy desiers shall be subject to thy husband, and he shall
rule over thee.

4. The displeasure of God, and his fearful anger conceived against us, John
3.36. He that obeieth not the son shall not see life, but the wrath of God
abides on him.

Nah. 3.6. And I will cast filth upon thee, and make thee vilde, and will set
thee as a gasing stock.

5. A privation of that admirable knowledge of God, and the nature of the
creatures, unto which we were created; so as we are all for horrible ignorance
almost like the beasts, in comparison of what once we might have had, Prou.
30.2. Surely I am more foolish then any man, and have not the understanding of
a man in me: and this light is wanting both to the mind, and the conscience.

6. Bondage to Satan, who has naturally strong holds in every man's heart, and
such spiritual possession, that having men in his snare, he leads them at
his pleasure, and works effectually both in them, and by them, Ephesians. 2.2.
Wherein in time past you walked according to the course of this world, and
after the Prince that rules in the air, even the spirit that now works in
the children of disobedience.

2. Tim. 2.26. And that they may come to amendment out of the snare of the
devil, which are taken of him at his will.

2. Cor. 10.5. Casting down the imaginations, and every high thing that is
exalted against the knowledge of God, etc.

7. Spiritual death, which comprehends in it the loss of communion with God
(the life of our lives), and all the joys of his favor and presence, together
with the obduratio^ of our hearts, which are become as a stone within us; so as
we are altogether insensible of the things that concern everlasting happiness.
Ephesians. 2.1. And you has he quickened, that were dead in trespasses and sins.

Ephesians. 4.18. Having their cogitation darkened, and being strangers from the
life of God, through the ignorance that is in them, because of the hardness of
their heart.

Ezech. 36.26. I will take away the stony heart out of your body, and I will
give you a heart of flesh.

8. Miserable bodies. Our bodies are become miserable, both in respect of
deformity, and in respect of imbecillitie; as also in respect of the many
pains befalles them, both from labor, and from diseases of all sorts, Genes.
3.13. In the sweat of thy face shall thou eat bread, till thou return to the
earth: for out of it wast thou taken, because thou art dust, and to dust shall
thou return, etc.

Deuteronomy. 28.21.22. The Lord shall make the pestilence cleave unto thee, until he
has consumed thee from the land, whether thou go to possess it.

The Lord shall smite thee with a consumption, and with the fever, and with a
burning ague, and with seruent heat, and with the sword, and with blasting, and
with the mildew, and they shall pursue thee, until thou perish, etc.

9. Judgments in our outward estates in temporal things by wars, famine,
fire, earthquakes, in-undations, ignominy, poverty, and such like of many
sorts, Deuteronomy. 28.16.17.18. etc. Cursed shall thou be in the town, and cursed
also in the field:

Cursed shall thy basket be, and thy dough:

Cursed shall be the fruit of thy body, and the fruit of thy land, the
increase of thy kine, and the flocks of thy sheep:

Cursed shall thou be when thou come in, and cursed also when thou go
out, etc.

10. The restraining of good things from us, even blessings of al sorts; and
that sometimes when they are by the free mercy of God bestowed upon others:
Isai. 59.2, But your iniquities have separated between you and your God, and
your sins have hid his face from you, that he will not hear. Job 31.2, for
what portion should I have of God from above? and what inheritance of the
Almighty from on high?

Act. 17.30. And the time of this ignorance God regarded not.

Ier. 5.25. Yet your iniquities have turned away these things, and your sins
have hindered good things from you, etc.

11. The cursing of blessings, when God blasts the good gifts he bestowed, or
suffers prosperity to become a snare, or trap, or ruin unto man, Mal. 2.2. I
will curse your blessings,

Ierem. 12.13. They have sown wheat, and reaped thorns, they have put
themselves to much pain, and had no profit: and they shall be ashamed of their
revenues, because of the fierce wrath of the Lord.

Psalm. 69.22. Let their table be a snare before them, and their prosperity
their ruin.

Prou. 1.26. I will also laugh at your destruction, and mock when your fear
comes etc.

12. Scourging of sin with sin, which is one of the most grievous
punishments; when God leaves a man so, as he suffers him to fall into
flagitious courses, and to commit sin with greediness; or delivers man up to a
reprobate mind, Romans 1.26.28. For this cause God gave them up unto vile
affections; for even their women did change the natural use, into that, which
is against nature.

For as they regarded not to know God, even so God delivered them up unto a
reprobate mind, to do those things which are not convenient.

13. Hellish terrors, which wound the soul with insupportable torments, many
times God softening the heart to feel inward smart, or suffering Satan to
torment the soul with unspeakable fears and horrors, Hebr. 10.27. But a
fearful looking-for of judgment and violent fire, which shall devour the
adversaries.

Esa. 33.14. The sinners in Sion are afraid, a fear is come upon the
hypocrites, who among us shall dwell with the devouring fire? who among us
shall dwell with the everlasting burnings?

Esa. 65.13.14. Therefore thus says the Lord, behold my servants shall eat,
and ye shall be hungry; behold my servants shall drink, and ye shall be
thirsty; behold my servants shall rejoice, and ye shall be ashamed.

Behold my servants shall sing for joy of heart, and ye shall cry for sorrow of
heart, and shall howl for vexation of mind.

14. Fear of death, which in some measure is in all, though the former be not;
every man being in that respect like a prisoner that is condemned, and looks
every day when he shall go to execution, Heb. 2.15. And that he might deliver
al^hem, which for fear of death were all their life time subject to bondage.

15. A terrible general judgment, when all men's sins shall be ripped up
before the whole world, to their eternal shame; and an order given for
unavoidable execution of the sentence, Act. 17.31. Because he has appointed a
day, in the which he will judge the world in righteousness, by that man, whom
he has appointed. etc.

16. A miserable departure, and loss of life, the soul and body being rent
asunder, and both losing for ever all the pleasures, or felicities of this
life; Romans 5.12. Wherefore as by one man sin entered into the world, and death
by sin; and so death went over al men, for as much as all men have sinned,
etc.

Romans 6.23. For the wages of sin is death.

17. Lastly, eternal pain: Now this eternal misery is lamentable, if we
consider, 1. either the degrees of it: 2. or the place: 3. or the continuance.

The degrees of damnation are;

1. First, they have no communion with God, nor participation in any of the
blessings of God, 2. Thessal. 1.9. Which shall be punished with everlasting
perdition from the presence of the Lord, and from the glory of his power* etc.

2. Secondly, they are united to the devil, with whom they have an eternal
fearful fellowship, Matthew. 25.41. Then shall he say unto them on the left
hand; depart from me ye cursed into everlasting fire, which is prepared for the
devil and all his angels.

3. They endure an unspeakable confusion, and most bitter ignominy, upon the
consideration of the discovery of their many shameful offenses.

4. They are inwardly affected with incredible horror, and torment of
conscience, arising from the sense of Gods anger for their sins, Esa. 30.33.
For Tophet is prepared of old; it is even prepared for the King; he has made
it deep and large; the burning thereof is fire and much wood, the breath of
the Lord, like a river of brimstone does kindle it.

Romans 2.8.9. But unto them that are contentious and disobey the truth, and obey
unrighteousness, shall be indignation and wrath.

Tribulation and anguish shall be upon the soul of every man that does evil:
of the Jew first, and also of the Grecian.

5. The bodies of the damned shall suffer inexpressible torments, which is set
out in Scriptures by their lying in fire and brimstone, Esa. 30.33. as
immediately before.

Luke 16.23. And being in hell torments, he lift up his eyes, and saw Abraham a
far off, and Lazarus in his bosom, etc.

Revel. 21.8. But the fearful and unbelieving, and the abominable, and
murderers, and whoremongers, and sorcerers, and Idolaters, and all liars,
shall have their part in the lake which burns with fire and brimstone, which
is the second death.

Matthew. 25.41. Then shall he say unto them on the left hand, Depart from me ye
cursed into everlasting fire, which is prepared for the devil and his angels.

This misery is increased by the fearfulnes of the place where it is to be
suffered, to which in diverse Scriptures, diverse names are given to intimate the
horror of it, as Hell, the pit, the great deep, or bottomless gulf, Prison,
Darkness, utter darkness, and many other terrible titles.

Matthew. 22.13. Then said the King to his servants, bind him hand and foot; take
him away, and cast him into utter darkness, there shall be weeping and
gnashing of teeth.

Revel. 20.1. And I saw an Angel come down from heaven, having the key of the
bottomless pit, and a great chain in his hand, etc.

And the smoke of their torment shall ascend evermore, and they shall have no
rest day nor night, etc.

Now follows the Uses.

The use may be first for singular reproof of the marvelous security of
multitudes of people, that can live quietly in so miserable a condition; were
not man sunk deep into rebellion, and besotted with unspeakable
senselessness, one would think it were impossible for him to eat, or sleep,
or ever to hold up his head. If we heard a story of the one half of these
distresses that were befallen another man, and did lay our hearts to it to
think tenderly of it, we could not but wonder, that that man could so forget
his own safety, as to neglect any means for his own release? but this very
observation shows two things, viz. that men are guilty of vile Atheism, and
unbelief, and of incredible Apathy, or insensiblenesse. Oh that men would but
think of these particulars, and ponder them seriously! but alas, a deceived
heart has seduced them, that they cannot say, here is my perdition, if I
repent not. And this reproof is aggrauated against some men in this, that they
are angry at any that shows them their danger, as we see by experience of men,
that live in gross sins: yet let the curses due to those sins be applied
to them, how do they rage? how are they like the very horse and mule, and much
worse?

sin, Ephesians. 5.14.
and learn to live righteously. 1. Cor. 15. Act. 17.31.
These Judgments may warn all men every where to repent: and seeing they are
thus undone by the first Adam, Romans 5.^2. etc.
to seek release from this dreadful misery by the second Adam; and ^.1. Mat.
11.29.
There is no condemnation to them that are in Christ Jesus; and there can be
no access to Christ without repentance from dead works, 1. Ioh. 2.1. Gal.
3.13, 2. Cor. 5.17.
and faith in him. Oh how were men sure to be freed by Christ, if they were
once weary and heavy laden! There is a full propitiation for all sin in him;
he has borne all that curse of the law, only if any man will be in Christ he
must be a new Creature.

This may instruct the godly,

1. The weak Christian should labor by all means to be established in the
faith, that as Christ has freed him from all these miseries (as curses), so
faith may free him from the fear of them; and to this end he should earnestly
and constantly pray, that God would make him worthy of his calling, and fulfill
all the good pleasure of his goodness, and the work of faith with power, 2.
Th. 1.11.12.

2. All Christians should forcibly compel upon themselves a careful practice
of 6. duties:

1. All ages should admire the exceeding riches of the tender kindness and
mercy of God, and the great love wherewith he has loved us, that has
forgiven us so great a debt, and freed us from so unspeakable confusion, Ephesians.
2.4.7.

2. We should often look upon Christ, that has borne all the malediction of
the law for us, and that both to move us to compassion, and mourning for our
sins, that so pierced him, Zach. 12.10. And also to settle our selves against
the fear of any of these miseries, seeing Christ has fully paid our debts,
and suffered the uttermost in our rooms: and further, if we did often set
before us that marvelous passion of our Lord and Savior, it might ravish our
hearts to a greater love toward him, and desire to be with him to give him
eternal thanks.

3. Have we escaped so much danger, which sin brought us into? Then let us
for ever be warned, and go our ways, and sin no more. Let us watch over our
selves, that we be not bewitched by the deceitfulnes of sin. For here we
may learn, that God can make sin extremely bitter unto us, but especially
let us leave sin, even because God has dealt so graciously with us.

4. It should teach us with all compassion to pity others with whom we
converse, that yet live in this misery, we should strive with all
effectualnesse of persuasion to draw them out of such an estate, and use our
uttermost power to pull them out of this fire, provoking them to holiness, and
good works, and exhorting and rebuking them with all instance, that they may
not perish in so great condemnation, Heb. 10.25.

5. It should teach us to endure all sorts of afflictions, yt God shall please
to try us withal, and that because they are no way comparable to the
punishments we are escaped from: and besides, God is pleased to cause them to
work our good: they try and increase our faith in Christ's merits: they make us
know our selves more thoroughly: they mollify and soften our hearts: they tame
our flesh: they scour our gifts from rust: they weane us from the world, and
excite the desire after, and care to provide for the world to come.

6. It should teach us with all gladness of heart to remember our miseries, as
waters that are past, and establish our selves in a daily solace, especially in
the expectation of the full and final deliverance from all the remnants of
distress in the day of Christ, when God shall be made marvelous in them that
believe, 2. These. 1.11. And the more we should lift up our heads, upon whom the
ends of the world are come, because the day of that redemption draws near.
Let us ever say with David, Psalm. 16.6. The lines are fallen upon me in
pleasant places: yea I have a fair heritage: Psa. 22.24.
and The Lord has drawn us out of many waters: let us therefore love the Lord
dearly, and rejoice always in the Lord, Phil. 4.4.

CHAP. XI. The estate of Grace.
Ephesians. 1.4. As he has chosen us in him, before the foundation of the world.


HItherto of the second estate of man.

The third estate is the estate of Grace, which is three ways to be
considered: 1. First, in respect of the means of the foundation of it. 2.
Secondly, in respect of the subject of the possession of it, which is the
Church. 3. Thirdly, in respect of the degrees of application, and
manifestation, which are two: viz. Justification, Sanctification.



The means of foundation is twofold.

1. Election in God: 2. Redemption in Christ.
Concerning Election, there are these evident Principles:

First, that there was a choice Election made by God, Ephesians. 1.4. As he has
chosen us in him, before the foundation of the world.

Secondly, that this choice was For ere the children were borne, and when they
had done neither good nor evil, that the purpose of God might remain
according to the Election, not by works, but by him that called, etc.

That only some men are Election? etc, Matthew. 20.16. Many are called, but few
chosen Mat. 22.14.

Election is the only free grace of God, not our works, Ephesians. 1.5. Who has
predestined us, to be adopted through Jesus Christ unto himself, according
to the good pleasure of his will, etc.

Romans 9.15.18. For he says unto Moses; I will have mercy on him, to whom I will
show mercy: and will have compassion on him, on whom I will have compassion.

Therefore he has mercy on whom he will, and whom he will, he hardneth.

Election is unchangeable, all the Elect shall be saved, Romans 8.30. Moreover,
whom he predestined, them also he called; and whom he called, them also he
justified; and whom he justified, them also he glorified, etc.

Isaiah 46.10. My Counsel shall stand, and I will do whatsoever I will.

2. Tim. 2.19. But the foundation of God remains sure, and h^th this seal;
The Lord knows who are his, etc.

John 6.37. All that the Father gives me, shall come to me; and him that
comes to me, I cast not away.

Matthew. 25.34. Then shall the King say to them on the right hand, Come ye
blessed of my Father; inherit ye the Kingdom prepared for you from the
foundations of the world.

The consideration of this doctrine of man's Election should teach us diverse
things:

Every one of us should study grace: now one labor does both, if we make our
calling sure, we make our Election sure, 2. Pet. 1. 10: and we may be sure our
calling is right, if we add virtue to our faith, if we can find the gifts of
grace in our hearts: for this (I fay) we must study the doctrine of the signs;
of which before.

Election, we should with all thankefulnes acknowledge Gods goodness to us,
and the riches of his free grace, as the Apostle teaches us, Ephesians. 1.3. and
2. These. 2.13. But we ought to give thanks always to the Lord for you brethren,
beloved of God, because that God has from the beginning chosen you to
salvation, through sanctification of the Spirit, and the faith of truth: and so
rest in this happiness, as our chief desire to God should be still to
vouchsafe us this favor to bless us with the favor of his chosen, Psalm.
106.4.5. Remember me, O Lord, with the favor of thy people, visit me with thy
salvation,

That I may see the felicity of thy chosen, and rejoice in the joy of thy
people, and glory with thine inheritance.

And for ever stand and gase at the marvelous riches of Gods grace, that
suffered us not to perish in the condemnation of the world.

Our Election should work upon And fashion not your selves like unto this
world, but be ye changed by the renewing of your mind, that ye may prove,
what is the good will of God, and acceptable, and perfect.

Deuteronomy. 14.2. For thou art an holy people unto the Lord thy God, and the Lord
has chosen thee to be a precious people unto himself above all the people,
that are upon the earth.

God has chosen us, and called us with a holy calling; and therefore we should
as a people peculiar unto him, be zealous of all good works, and show forth
the virtues of him that called us, and walk before him with all desire to
please him, that has thus Elected us; we should ever be ready to choose the
Lord to be our God, and to show it by auouching him, and by walking in his
ways, as these Scriptures plentifully show.

Deuteronomy. 7.6.7. For thou art an holy people unto the Lord thy God, the Lord thy
God has chosen thee to be a precious people unto himself, above all the people
that are upon the earth.

The Lord does not set his love upon you, nor choose you, because ye were more
in number then any people: for ye were the fewest of all people.

Deuteronomy. 26.16.17. This day the Lord thy God has commanded thee to do these
ordinances and laws, keep them therefore, and do them with all thine heart,
and with all thy soul.

Thou have set up the Lord this day to be thy God, and to walk in his ways,
and to keep his ordinances, and his commandments, and his laws, and to
hearken to his voice.

Ephesians. 1.4. As he has chosen us in him before the foundation of the world,
that we should be holy, and without blame before him in love.

1. Pet. 2.9.16. But ye are a chosen generation, a roial Priesthood, an holy
Nation, a peculiar people, that ye should show forth the virtues of him, that
has called you out of darkness into his marvelous light.

As free, and not as having the liberty for a cloak of maliciousnes, but as
the servants of God.

We should give our names to God, as they that will subscribe and deuote
themselves only to the God of Jacob, Isaiah 44.1.5. Yet now hear, O Jacob, my
servant, and Israel, whom I have chosen.

One shall say, I am the Lord; another shall be called by the name of Jacob;
and another shall subscribe with his hand unto the Lord, and name himself by
the name of Israel.

4. It should teach us to imitate God, and choose the godly, as the persons we
would most observe, admire, love, defend, and live withal, Ioh. 15.17. These
things command I you, that ye love one another. John 17.26. And I have
declared unto them thy name, and will declare it, that the love wherewith thou
have loved me, may be in them, and I in them, etc. Yea we should not have the
glorious faith of Christ, in respect of persons to despise poor Christians,
and only respect great men: for God has chosen the weak things of this world
to confound the mighty, and the poor he has chosen to be made heirs of the
Kingdom, and rich in faith, James 2.5. 1. Cor. 1.27. Yea, we should be
content, as the Apostle says, to suffer all things for the Elects sake, seeing
they are so dear to God, 2. Tim. 2.10.

We may know our Election by two sorts of signs: First, the one respects God:
Secondly, the other respects our selves. God declares his eternal choice by
diverse marks of it, and man proves himself to be Elect of God by diverse tokens
of it.

God shows whom he has chosen from everlasting three manner of ways:

1. By Election in time, when God separates a man from the world unto himself
and his service: It is a manifest sign of Election: it shows an eternal
choice, when God singles a man out from the multitude of carnal and careless
men, and inspires him with an unchangeable resolution to deuote himself to
God: it is an evident declaration of Gods predestination to glory; God
separates a man from the world, when he makes him a weary of wicked and
unprofitable society; and takes away from him the taste in earthly things, so
as the love of the world is not in him, and sanctifies him to his own use.

2. By the entertainment God gives them in his house, and especially by the
efficacy of the word, and principally by the life of the promises: for God
makes his word a word of power, and the holy Ghost falls upon their hearts,
and they at sometimes feel a marvelous assurance in hearing, and so much
comfort, that they can receive the word, though it be with much affliction, and
rejoice greatly in it; and the word transformes them also to a constant desire
of practice, and imitation of the godliness of the Saints, 1. These. 1.4.5.6.
Knowing, beloved brethren, that ye are Elect of God:

For our Gospel was not unto you in word only, but also in power, and in the
holy Ghost, and in much assurance:

And ye became followers of us, and of the Lord, and received the word in much
affliction, with joy of the holy Ghost.

Psalm. 65.4. Blessed is he whom thou chusest, and causest to come to thee, he
shall dwell in thy courts, and we shall be satisfied with the pleasures of thine
house even thy holy temple.

Romans 9.8.11. That is, they which are the children of the flesh, are not the
children of God: but the children of promise are counted for the seed.

3. By the sanctification of their afflictions, even by the many experiences of
Gods love in afflictions, as when God comforts their hearts in the midst of
distress, when they come to him making their moan; and when he turns the
cross to a blessing to them, making them more humble by it, exercising their
gifts, purging out their sin, etc. and at the length giving gracious
deliverances, causing all to work together for the best, so as they themselves
being Judges, they can say it was good for me, that I was afflicted, Romans
8.28.29. Also we know, that all things work together for the best to them that
love God, even to them that are called of his purpose, etc.

Psalm. 119. in many places.

Now as God manifests his own choie by these and such like signs; so the
godly make sure their own election by diverse marks of it, as generally by the
sanctification of the Spirit, and belief of the truth, 2. These. 2.13. But we
ought to give thanks always to God for you brethren, beloved of the Lord,
because that God has from the beginning chosen you to salvation through
sanctification of the Spirit, and the faith of truth, so in particular.

1. By the virtues of Christ, which more or less in some measure shine in
them, such as are humility, piety, knowledge, temperance, and contempt of the
world patience in adversity, and other excellent saving graces in them, 2.
Pet. 1.5.6.7.10. 1. Pet. 2.9. By their fruits you may know them, Ioh. 15.16.

2. Secondly, by the affections of godliness, that are in them above al
others, Ephesians. 1.5. 1. Ioh. 3.14. They approve themselves to be elect by love;
that is, by their great affections to God, to the word of God, and his
ordinances, and by their brotherly kindness to the godly, and this love is the
more evident mark, when it lasts even in affliction, when no distresses makes
us abate of our affection to God, or good things, or good men, Romans 8.28.

3. By their Priesthood: Gods elect are a kingdom of Priests, they offer God
daily sacrifice, they have the spirit of prayer, and they daily mortify (the
beast) their sins upon the Altar of Christ crucified. So then by their
