10. As many as are under the works of the law, are under the curse, etc.

23. Before faith came, we were kept under the law, and shut up, etc.

2. Of the most of us, for leaning still too much to our own works; we can
hardly tell, how, in our either glorying, or grieuing, to quit our selves from
the infection of pleading merit of works.

3. Of many dear servants of God for their slothfulness, and miserable
neglect of the assurance of faith; resting still in their weakness of faith,
and not striving to be fully persuaded.

CHAP. XXV. Of Sanctification.
1. These. 4.4. For this is the will of God, even your sanctification.


HItherto of Justification; Sanctification follows. Concerning Sanctification
there are these principles:

1. That whom God justifies, he sanctifies, Romans 8.30. Moreover whom he
predestinate, them also he called, and whom he called, them also he
justified, and whom he justified, them he also glorified.

Ezech. 36.26.27. etc. A new heart also will I give you, and a new spirit will
I put within you, and I will take away the stony heart out of your body, and I
will give you an heart of flesh.

And I will put my spirit within you, and cause you to walk in my statutes,
and ye shall keep my judgments and do them, etc.

2. That to be truly sanctified, is to die to sin, and to rise again to
newness of life, Romans 6.1.2.3.4. What shall we say then? shall we continue in
sin, that grace may abound? God forbid: how shall we that are dead to sin,
live yet therein?

Know ye not, that all we which have bin baptized into Jesus Christ, have been
baptized into his death?

We are buried then with him by baptism into his death, that like as Christ
was raised up from the dead by the glory of the Father; so we also should walk
in newness of life, etc. Or it is to repent and believe the Gospel, Mark.
1.15. The time is fulfilled, and the kingdom of God is at hand: repent, and
believe the Gospel.

3. That except we be borne again, we cannot enter into the kingdom of God,
Ioh. 3.5. Jesus answered, verily, verily I say unto thee, except that a man be
borne of water and of the spirit, he cannot enter into the kingdom of God.

Heb. 12.14. Follow peace with all men, and holiness, without the which no man
shall see the Lord.

1. Ioh. 1.7. But if we walk in the light, as he is in the light, we have
fellowship one with another, and the blood of Jesus Christ his Son cleanses
us from all sin.

2. Cor. 5.17. Therefore if any man be in Christ, let him be a new creature:
old things are passed away, behold all things are become new.

Fourthly, that sanctification is Gods gift, and work in Jesus Christ; we can
no more convert our selves, then we can beget our selves at first: we can no
more create our selves new men, then we can create our selves men, Act. 5.31.
Him has God lifted up with his right hand to be a Prince, and a Savior, to
give repentance to Israel, and forgiveness of sins.

Act. 11.18. When they heard these things, they held their peace, and glorified
God saying: then has God also to the Gentiles granted repentance unto life.

2. Tim. 2.25. Instructing them with meeknes, that are contrary minded; proving
if God at any time will give them repentance, that they may know the truth.

1. Cor. 1.30. But ye are of him in Christ Jesus, who of God is made unto us
wisdom, and righteousness, and sanctification and redemption.

Ezech. 37.28. Thus the heathen shall know, that I the Lord do sanctify
Israel, when my sanctuary shall be amongst them for evermore.

Tit. 3.5. Not by the works of righteousness which we had done, but
according to his mercy he saved us by the washing of the new birth, and the
renewing of the holy Ghost.

Fifthly, that our sanctification is imperfect, while we live in this world,
1. Ioh. 1.8. If we say that we have no sin, we deceive our selves, and the
truth is not in us.

Prou. 24.16. For a just man falls seven times and rises again: but the
wicked fall into mischief.

Esa. 64.6. But we have all been as an unclean thing, and all our righteousness
is as filthy clouts; and we do all fade like a leaf, and our iniquities like
the wind have taken us away.

The uses may be for Information: Instruction: Humiliation: and Consolation.


For the first: we may here take notice of the wisdom of God in curing the
posterity of Adam. We received a double disease from Adam: the one was guilt
of eternal death: the other was corruption of nature. By Justification the
first was abolished, and by Sanctification the other is healed by degrees.

For the second, we may here learn many things:

The first is carefully to study our own sanctification, and compel upon our
selves a more constant endeavor of sound reformation. To this end I propound
two things:

1. Certain motives which we should have continually in our minds, to stir
us up to the care of holiness, and to get true grace.

2. Certain rules, which may exceedingly further us about our Sanctification.

The motives are these, amongst many:

1. The commandment of God, 1. These. 4.3. This is the will of God, even your
sanctification.

Ephesians. 2.10. For we are his workmanship, created in Christ Jesus unto good
works, which God has ordained that we should walk in them.

2. The conscience of our debt, which we owe herein, Romans 8.12. Therefore
brethren we are debtors, not to the flesh to live after the flesh: being
redeemed by Christ.

Tit. 2.14. Who gave himself for us, that he might redeem us from all
iniquity, and purge us to be a peculiar people to him self, zealous of good
works.

3 The consideration of our own dignity: we are the children of God, the
temples of the holy Ghost, Kings and Priests unto God; Gods own peculiar
people and inheritance.

4. The rich promises that belong to godliness, 1. Tim. 4.8. For bodily
exercise profits little: but godliness is profitable unto all things, which
has the promise of the life present, and of that that is to come.

5. The assuring hereby of our calling, and Election, 2. Pet. 1.10. Wherefore
brethren, give rather diligence to make your calling and election sure: for if
ye do these things, ye shall never fall.

6. The excellency of good works: they are sacrifices seasoned with the salt
of faith, kindled with the fire of the holy Ghost, offered by the merit of
Christ, and accepted of God, 1. Pet. 2.5. And ye be made a holy Priesthood, to
offer up spiritual sacrifices acceptable to God by Jesus Christ.

7. The silencing of the ignorant from speaking evil, 1. Pet. 2.15. For so is
the will of God, that by well doing ye may put to silence the ignorance of the
foolish.

8. Because else,

1. The name of God will be blasphemed, Romans 2.24. For the name of God is
blasphemed among the Gentiles, through you.

2. Sam. 12.14. Howbeit because by this deed thou have caused the enemies of
the Lord to blaspheme, the child that is borne unto thee shall surely die, etc.

2. The spirit of God will be grieved, and the works of the spirit deaded,
Ephesians. 4.30. And grieve not the holy spirit of God, by whom ye are sealed unto
the day of redemption.

3. The judgment of God will be provoked, Psalm. 89.31.32.

The rules we had need to be put in mind of, that concern Sanctification,
either show us what to take heed of, or what to do.

That we be not deceived in this great work of true grace, we must take heed,

First, of wretchlesnesse and security, whereby a man lives so, as he is
insensible and careless of reformation altogether. Awake thou that sleep,
Ephesians. 5.14.

Secondly, of the daily baits, and methods of sin: be not ensnared with the
pleasures of sin, which are but for a season; but circumcise betimes the
soreskins of your hearts, Ier. 4.4.

Thirdly, of procrastination, and delaying of time in the business of
reformation. For thy life is uncertain, Matthew. 25.13. and every day adds to
the heap of sin, and of wrath, Romans 2.5. Sin not against thy purposes of
amendment, lest thou grow more hardened.

Fourthly, of hypocrisy, and fained holiness, Esa. 58.2. Iam. 4.8.

Fifthly, of the persuasion of the merit of your own works, Romans 10.3. For
they being ignorant of the righteousness of God, and going about to stablish
their own righteousness, have not submitted themselves to the righteousness
of God etc.

Sixthly, of temporary righteousness, Hosh. 6.4. Ephraim, what shall I do unto
thee? O Judah, how shall I entreat thee? for your goodness is as a morning cloud,
and as a morning dew it goes away. Or being weary of well doing, Gal. 6.9. Let
us not therefore be weary of well doing: for in due season we shall reap, if
we faint not, etc.

Seventhly, of the precepts of men, Mat. 15.9. In vain they worship me,
teaching for doctrine men's precepts.

Ezech. 20.18. But I said unto their children in the wilderness, walk ye not in
the ordinances of your fathers, neither observe their manners, nor defile your
selves with their idols.

Eighthly, of looking after the example, and fashion of the world, Romans 12.2.
Frame not your selves like unto this world.

Ninthly, neglect of prayer for the particular furtherance of reformation and
grace, Lam. 5.21. shall he not give us his holy Spirit, if we ask him, as our
Savior shows in the parable?

Tenthly, let the best of us take heed of a strange deceit, and that is to rest
in fair words, and attentive hearing. How is it, that men, that hear many
precious counsels, comforts, and reproves, go away without any reformation,
and think they do well, if they commend the Sermon? etc. Oh, how common is
this disease to be awake to hear of the disease, or medicine, and fall a
sleep before it be applied? like those hearers in the Gospel, of whom it is
said, They heard, they marvelled, and they went their ways.

Thus much of what we should avoid, that the work of sanctification be not
hindered.

On the other side there be diverse things to be observed by us, as

First, we must look to the matter to be done, which has two considerations
in it:

1. That in general whatsoever things are true, honest, just, pure, lovely,
and of good report, that have virtue and praise in them, that we should think
on those things, and study how to glorify God, and enrich our selves by well
doing them, Phil. 4.8. Ephesians. 58. etc.

2. That we strive to keep our selves free from, or speedily mortify such
evils as usually stain the profession of religion after calling. Besides the
mortification of gross evils, which the first repentance puts away; we must
watch carefully against other sins, such as are lying, rotten communication,
deceit, anger, wrath, and all bitterness, and cursed speaking, Col. 3.8.
Ephesians 4.25.

Secondly, we must look to the end of all our actions, the end I say both of
intention, and continuance: For

1. We must propound the glory of God, as the maine end of all our actions,
1. Cor. 10.31. Whether therefore ye eat or drink, or whatsoever ye do, do
all to the glory of God. Philip. 1.11.

2. We must so begin reformation and good works, as we be sure also to
endeavor with all constancy to hold out to the end, Luke 1.75. All the days of
our life in holiness and righteousness before him.

Psalm. 106.3. Blessed are they that keep judgment, and do righteousness at
all times.

Thirdly, we must look to the manner of our reformation, that it be done with
all sincerity, and so we do,

1. If we turn from all sorts of our transgressions, Ezech. 18. 30.31.
Therefore I will judge you, O House of Israel, every one according to his
ways; return therefore, and cause other to turn away from all your
transgressions, so iniquity shall not be your destruction.

Cast away from you all your transgressions, whereby ye have transgressed, and
make you a new heart, and a new spirit: for why will ye die, O House of Israel?

2. If we labor for a sanctification that is throughout in all parts, in
soul, in body, and in spirit, that is, in our outward man, and in our
affections, and in our judgments, and thoughts.

Fourthly, we must be exceeding mindful of the means of sanctification, and
so we must especially think of

1. The Word, to subject our selves to the power of it: for if we hear our
souls shall live, we are sanctified by the truth, and God will have his Law
magnified, and the Word is able to build us up still further, till we come to
heaven, Isai. 55.4. John 17.19. Isaiah 42.21. Acts 20.32.

2. The Sabbath: for that is the sign of our sanctification. It is a sign to
assure, that God will not fail us in his blessings; and it is a sign that we
are indeed a holy people, if we be careful to keep the Sabbath. It is the
market day for our souls, and by the right keeping of the Sabbath, we shall be
the better able to serve God all the week after, Exodus 31.13. 14. Keep ye my
Sabbaths: for it is a sign between me and you in your generation, that ye may
know, that I the Lord do sanctify you.

Ye shall therefore keep the Sabbath, for it is holy unto you; he that
defiles it shall die the death: therefore whosoever works therein, the same
person shall be even cut off from among his people.

Isaiah 56.2. Blessed is the man that does this, and the son of man which
lays hold on it: he that keeps the Sabbath, and polluteth it not, and
keeps his hand from doing any evil, etc.

Thus of the uses for instruction.

Thirdly, these principles may terrify all men that are unsanctified, that
have not true grace, that live in their sins: Woe unto worlds of men because
of sin! for thereby they may gather, that there is no cure done to their
natures, that they are not at all justified before God, that they have no part
with Christ, and that all they do is still impure, Mat. 7.18. Tit. 1.15. Yea,
and that the wages of their sins will be death, and that in the state they
are in, they cannot be saved, Romans 6.23. John 3.5. and in the mean time, what
know they how soon the whirlwind of the Lord may fall upon the wicked? Ier.
23.19. Behold, the tempest of the Lord goes forth in his wrath and a violent
whirlwind shall fall down upon the head of the wicked.

And for all the things they have done in the flesh, they must come to
judgment; and the rather because they have not taken warning, Acts 17.31.
Because he has appointed a day* in the which he will judge the world in
righteousness by that man, whom he has appointed, etc.

Object. But some one may say, what tell ye us of these terrible things? we
have no reason to think of our selves, that we are unsanctified, how can we,
or you tell, who are not sanctified?

Sol. It is easy to tell in the negative, who are not sanctified, you may know
it of wicked men:

1. Because they are a sleep, and dead in sin, and have not not any true
feeling of the hatefulness of their many sins, Ephesians. 2.1. And you has he
quickened, that were dead in trespasses and sins.

2. Because sin reigns in them, it has an unlimited power in them, Romans
6.12. Let not sin reign therefore in your mortal body, that ye should obey
it in the lusts thereof.

3. Because they sin by covenant, they hire themselves; their purpose is with
their whole hearts to commit and continue in sin, they obey as servants, Romans
6.16. Know ye not, that to whomsoever ye give your selves, as servants to
obey, his servants ye are to whom ye obey, whether it be of sin unto death,
or of obedience unto righteousness.

4. Because they are silent from prayer, and confession of sin, Psalm.
32.23.5.

5. Because they have no savor of the things of the spirit, but altogether
savor fleshly things, Romans 8.5. For they that are after the flesh, savor the
things of the flesh: but they that are after the spirit, the things of the
spirit.

6. Because they never had any marriage affections to Jesus Christ, Romans 7.5.

7. Lastly, a wicked man finds in himself not only an impotency, but an
impossibility to be subject to the Law of God. He resolves, that he cannot
possibly yield to the directions of the word, nor will not: whereas a godly
mind loves the Law, desires to obey, endeavors it, subjects himself to it,
though he fail many ways.

Fourthly and lastly, the godly may be comforted in the observation of this
work of the spirit of grace, that is in Jesus Christ, which killes sin in
them, and has made them alive from the dead.

Object. But some weak Christian might say, There is much comfort in this
doctrine of the healing of their natures, save that the imperfection of their
sanctification is a continual discomfort.

Solut. Christians may and ought to comfort themselves against the imperfection
of their sanctification many ways, and so if they look

1. Upon the Spirit of God in their hearts, and so two things may relieve them;
first the assistance of the Spirit, which will help their infirmities, Romans 8.
26. And then if they consider the very fountain of all good actions, and every
good gift to be the same spirit of God, they must needs conclude, it is some
divine thing which is wrought in them, in as much as it flows from the holy
Ghost; howsoever it be imperfect through the corruption of their hearts.

2. Upon Jesus Christ; and so if they behold,

1. His intercession, and that likewise has a double comfort in it: for first
Christ made intercession for us, when he prayed for our sanctification, it
should much comfort us to remember, that our sanctification was one of the
things Christ prayed for, John, 17.19. Secondly, Christ in his intercession in
heaven, couers all the imperfections of the godly, and is their advocate before
the Father, 1. John, 2.2. Romans 8.34.

2. His death and resurrection, from whence flows a virtue continually, which
is of singular power, to make our sins still die in us, and quicken us to
newnes of life. Romans 6.4. For this cause did Christ sanctify himself, that
he might sanctify his members by the influence come from him, as from their
head, John, 17.17.

3. Upon the hope of perfect holiness: for the time will come, when they shall
be without spot, or wrincle, Ephesians. 5.27. The merit of their perfect holiness
is found in the price paid by Jesus Christ, Heb. 10.14. It should much solace
them, that one day there shall be a perpetual end of all sin and infirmities.

4. If in the mean time they look upon the good nature of God, assuring them
by his promises,

1. That they are under Grace, and not under the Law, Romans 6.14.

2. That he will not deal with us after our sins, Psalm. 103.

3. That he will spare us, as a man spares his son that serves him, Mal.
3.17.

4. That he will accept of the will and desire for the deed, 2. Cor. 8.12.

5. That he is slow to anger, and ready to forgive, Psalm. 103.8. And mercy
pleases him, Micha. 7.18.

6. That he will pass by our infirmities, and mere frailties, and not take
notice of them, Micha. 7.18.

CHAP. XXVI. Of the Resurrection.
Ioh. 5.28.29. Marvel not at this: for the hour shall come, in the which all
that are in the graves, shall hear his voice:

And they shall come forth that have done good, unto the resurrection of life;
but they that have done evil, unto the resurrection of condemnation.


HItherto of the principles that concern the third estate of man.

The fourth estate of man is the estate of glory; and in this we are to
consider the three degrees of it: 1. The Resurrection of the the body. 2. The
last Judgment. 3. The glory of Heaven.


The principles concerning the resurrection are these:

First, that the bodies of dead men shall rise out of the dust of the earth,
and their own souls shall enter into them again, Job 19.23.26. For I am sure
that my Redeemer lives, and he shall stand the last on the earth.

And though after my skin worms destroy this body, yet shall I see God in my
flesh.

Esa. 26.19. Thy dead men shall live; even with my body shall they rise: Awake
and sing ye that dwell in dust: for thy dew is as the dew of herbs, and the
earth shall cast out the dead, etc.

Ioh. 5.28. Marvel not at this, for the hour shall come, in the which all
that are in the graves, shall hear his voice.

1. Cor. 15.16. For if the dead be not raised, then is Christ not raised, etc.
in the whole chapter.

Secondly, yt the bodies of all men shall be raised, Ioh. 5.28. as before.
Small and great; the earth, sea, fire, beasts, fowls, air, etc. shall deliver
up their dead, Revel. 20.12.13. And I saw the dead, both great and small, stand
before God; and the books were opened, and another book was opened, which is
the book of life, and the dead were judged of those things which were written
in the books, according to their works.

And the sea gave up her dead which were in her, and death and hell delivered
up the dead which were in them, and they were judged every man according to
their works. Just and unjust shall rise, Act. 24.15. And have hope toward God,
that the resurrection of the dead, which they themselves look for also, shall
be both of just, and unjust. Though the unjust shall not rise in the same
manner, nor by the same power, that is, by the virtue of Christ's resurrection,
Dan. 12.2. And many of them that sleep in the dust of the earth shall awake,
some to everlasting life, and some to shame and perpetual contempt.

Quest. It may be objected, that Daniel says many shall rise, not all.

Answ. He may speak so, because we shall not all die; but those that are
alive at Christ's coming, shall be changed in stead of death and resurrection,
1. These. 4.15. For this say we unto you by the word of the Lord, that we which
live, and are remaining in the coming of the Lord, shall not prevent them
which sleep, etc. 1. Cor. 15.53.

Thirdly, that the same bodies, which men carry about with them in this world
shall rise again, Job 19.26.27. And though after my skin worms destroy this
body, yet shall I see God in my flesh.

Whom I my self shall see, and mine eyes shall behold, and none other for me,
though my raines are consumed within me.

Psalm. 34.20. He keeps all his bones, not one of them is broken.

This very corruptible must put on incorruption, 1. Cor. 15. 53. For this
corruptible must put on incorruption, and this mortal must put on immortality,
etc.

The reasons are, 1. because every man shall receive in his body, what he has
done, either good or evil, 2. Cor. 5.10. For we must all appear before the
judgment seat of Christ, that every man may receive the things which are done
in his body, according to that he has done, whether good or evil.

2. Because else it were absurd that any other body should be crowned, but
that which suffered: or punished, but that which sinned.

Fourthly, that this resurrection shall be at the end of the world, even the
last day of the world, Ioh. 6.44. No man can come to me, except the Father
which has sent me, draw him: and I will raise him up at the last day.

And therefore we must distinguish between particular resurrections, and the
general or universal. Particular resurrections have been past in some cases
miraculously, as at the time of Christ's death: but the principle speaks of the
universal resurrection.

The uses may be for Information. Instruction. Consolation. Terror.


First, for information, and so we should strive to inform our selves in three
things: 1. The certainty of it, that it shall surely be. 2. The manner of it,
since it must needs be. 3. The glory of the life in Christ, that can effect
this.


For the first, we may find many ways to affect our hearts with a full
assurance that our dead bodies shall rise again: many things tend hereunto,
some probable, some infallible, some show it that it may be, others that it
shall be.

That it is not impossible, other works in nature show: as first, the Phoenix,
a bird in Arabia, of which it is written, that waxing old, with the sticks of
Frankincense and Cassia, with which she filled her nest, she makes a fire,
and being put in the fire, and burned to ashes, by and by after the dew of
heaven lights upon her, she comes forth alive. Secondly, we know that many
little birds, which for the wintertime lie out of the way in deep marshes, or
such like places; yet in spring time come out alive again. Thirdly, we see
that trees, and plants in winter loose all their ornaments, and being dead to
see to, yet revive again. Fourthly, thus does the seed also which the
husbandman throws into the ground, 1. Cor. 15.36. O fool, that which thou
sowest is not quickened except it die. Fifthly and lastly, night and day,
sleep and waking, shows us thus much: the day dies into the night, and yet
reuiues to the world with all his glory.

Yea in man himself there is grounds of singular probability: For,

First his deliverances, from dangers and distresses, are (as it were) lesser
resurrections, and the term is given to it. The houses in which the Jews were
captives, were as so many graves; and their return, as a rising from the dead,
Ezech. 37.12. 2. Cor. 1.10.

Secondly, he has had an experience of the first resurrection in his soul
already, and how can he doubt the rising of his body? Romans 6. Ioh. 5.25.28.
Reu. 20.6.

Thirdly, diverse particular men have appeared raised from the dead; as Lazarus,
Ioh. 13.43. the Saints that appeared out of the graves after Christ's death,
Mat. 27.52.53.

Fourthly, God showed this in a vision to Ezechiel, when he saw a field full of
dry bones, receiving at Gods commandment flesh, and nerves, and life, Ezech.
37.

But we have more then probabilities, we have certain arguments for it, as

First, the word of God assuring it, 1. These. 4.15. as was proved before, to
whom all things are possible, Luke 1.37. For with God shall nothing be
impossible, Luke 18.27. The things which are impossible with men, are possible
with God. Romans 4.21.

Secondly, the Son of God undertaking to effect it, John 6. 39. And this is
the Fathers will which has sent me, that of all which he has given me, I
should loose nothing, but should raise it up again at the last day, etc.

Thirdly, the resurrection of Christ to assure it, who rose as our surety, 1.
These. 4.14.

Fourthly, the Sacrament of Baptizme seals both the resurrection of soul and
body.

Fifthly and lastly, the Apostle proves at large the necessity of the
resurrection, by many arguments: showing in effect, that all religion is
ouerturned, if the resurrection be not believed, 1. Cor. 15.12.

Thus that it shall be: How it shall be, follows.

The manner of the resurrection will be thus:

First, when the last day of the world is come, Christ on a sudden, in the same
visible form he went to heaven, will come in the clouds with his Angels, and
thousands of the souls of his Saints, Jude 14. 1. These. 4.15.

Secondly, the trumpet of God shall then sound, the voice of the Arch-angell
shall then be heard: Christ shall command, What these things mean is unknown.
exhort, and call upon the dead to rise and come away to judgment, 1. These.
4.16.17. so as the very dead shall hear this shout and voice of Christ, Ioh.
5.29. Matthew. 24.31.

Thirdly, immediately the spirit of Christ will bring the souls of all the
godly, and they shall enter into their bodies; and then they that have slept in
the dust of the earth, shall be raised to life.

Fourthly, the bodies of the wicked shall then be raised also by the power of
God, by a way unknown.

Fifthly, men, that shall then be alive, shall have a change on a sudden in stead
of death, and resurrection, 1. Cor. 15. 1. These. 4.15. 16.

Sixthly, the Angels shall then gather the Elect, and chase in the reprobates
from the four winds of heaven, and present them before Christ, Matthew. 24.31.
Thus of the manner.

Thirdly, this may inform us concerning the glorious life of the Son of God,
who does not only live himself; but gives life to millions of men by his
spirit, Ioh. 5.21. and raised dead bodies so miraculously.

Thus of the uses for information.

From the doctrine of the resurrection we should learn diverse things.

First, it should teach us not to mourn immoderatly for the dead, since when
Christ comes again, he will bring them with him; and the earth and seas shall
make a true account of their dead in the day of Christ, 1. These. 4.13.14.

Secondly, it should teach us to have the very body in honor, and not to
transgress against it, seeing it is redeemed by Christ, and shall be raised to
immortality at the last day.

Now men sin against the body:

1. When (according to the traditions of men, and through will worship) they
withhold from the body due sustenance, Col. 2.23.

2. When men pollute their bodies, that should be prepared to immortality, with
filthiness; such as is whoredom, drunkenness, sodomitry, and such like
abominations, 1. Cor. 6.13.14.

3. When the bodies of the Saints are not carefully and with meet honor
buried, or their burying places uncivilly dis-regarded.

Thirdly, the consideration of this great work of the resurrection of men's
bodies, should teach us to trust God in lesser matters, and believe his
promises, though there be never so great unlikelihood of the accomplishment,
in respect of outward means and appearance. Romans 4.17.18.

Fourthly, we should especially be careful to get the assurance, that our
bodies shall have a glorious resurrection, Act. 24.15. And that we may be so
assured:

1. We must pray God to give us his holy spirit, as the pledge of it. For then
if the spirit of Christ be in us, the same spirit that raised Christ, will
raise up our natural bodies at the last day, Romans 8.11.

2. We must be sure of the first resurrection, that the body be dead in
respect of sin, and the soul raised up to a lively care of newness of life:
Rise first in soul.
they that have their part in the first resurrection, shall never taste of the
second death, Romans 6. Revel. 20.6.

3. In particular, we must be sure to get faith in Jesus Christ, who is the
resurrection, and the life, and in whom whosoever believes, he shall not die
for ever, Ioh. 11.25.

Fifthly, we should resolve to live, like such as believe a glorious
Resurrection, and to this end

1. We should be steadfast, and immovable in all conditions of life, 1. Cor.
15.58.

2. We should live, as men devoted wholly to the service of Jesus Christ, whose
we are both in life and death, Romans 14.7.8.

3. We should strive to abound in the work of the Lord, 1. Cor. 15.58. rousing
up our selves to the care of well doing, 1. Cor. 15. 34. studying to keep a
conscience void of offense toward God and man, Acts 24.16.

4. Our minds should run on that time, and our conversation should be in
heaven, Philip. 3.20.

Thus much of the uses for instruction.

Thirdly, the doctrine of the resurrection has singular comfort in it, and
Christians are charged to comfort themselves, and one another with these
things, 1. These. 4.18. And David did rejoice, and was glad at heart for this
reason, Psalm. 16.9. For that is the time of the refreshing of all Christians,
Acts 3.19. And so the godly have been wont to comfort themselves against diverse
maladies, as

1. Against the pains and tortures of the body; so did Job, Job, 19.25.26.27.
For I am sure, that my Redeemer lives, and he shall stand the last on earth.

And though after my skin, worms destroy this body; yet shall I see God in my
flesh.

Whom I my self shall see, and mine eyes shall behold, and none other for me,
though my reins are consumed within me.

And so did the godly mentioned, Heb. 11.35. The women received their dead
raised to life; other also were racked, and would not be delivered, that they
might receive a better resurrection.

2. Against the troubles and general miseries of this life, and so Gods people
are comforted, Dan. 12.1.2. And at that time shall Michael stand up, the great
Prince which stands for the children of thy people; and there shall be a time
of trouble, such as was never since there began to be a nation unto the same
time; and at that time thy people shall be delivered, every one that shall be
found written in the book.

And many of them that sleep in the dust of the earth, shall awake, some to
everlasting life, and some to shame and perpetual contempt.

Isaiah 26.19. Thy dead men shall live; even with my body shall they rise:
Awake, and sing ye that dwell in dust; for thy dew is, as the dew of herbs,
and the earth shall cast out the dead.

3. Against death it self, and so the Apostle triumphs, 1. Cor. 15.55.56.57. O
Death where is thy sting! O grave, where is thy victory!

The sting of death is sin: and the strength of sin is the Law.

But thanks be unto God, which has given us victory through our Lord Jesus
Christ.

Object. Now if any ask, What in the doctrine of the resurrection should
comfort us in those cases?

Solut. I answer: The consideration of the marvelous glory of our bodies, in
which they should rise, should fill us with sweet refreshings, Phil. 3.21. Who
shall change our vile body, that it may be fashioned like unto his glorious
body, according to the working, whereby he is able to subdue al things unto
himself. For six things shall befall our bodies at that day:

1. Immortality: so as they can never die again, 1. Cor. 15.42.43.44.53.

2. Incorruptiblenesse: they shall never be inclined to putrefaction, or any
corruption.

3. Spiritualnesse: our bodies shall be raised spiritual bodies; they shall
be like spirits, as it were, and that in diverse respects:

1. Because they shall be possessed fully by the Spirit of God, so as they
shall be both governed by the Spirit, and be subject to the Spirit wholly.

2. Because they shall live as the Angels in heaven do, without meat or
raiment, or any other bodily helps or sustenance.

3. Because they shall be for nimblenesse, as it were spirits; they shall be
able with incredible swiftness, to pass into all the parts of the world,
earth, or air, etc. for they shall meet Christ in the air, 1. Thessal. 4.17.

4. Power: for of bodies full of weakness, and subject to many calamities and
distresses, and pains, they shall be raised in power; that is, strong, able,
and impassible.

5. Perfection: for they shall be freed from deformity, vnhandsomnesse,
maimes, lamenesse, etc. and become most fair and comely; neither infancy, nor
old age hindering them, but shall appear in full age and beauty.

6. Shining and splendour, as the Sun or Stars in the Firmament: the body
being clothed with a celestial glory and divine light, 1. Cor. 15.40. Dan.
12.3. And they that be wise, shall shine as the brightness of the Firmament;
and they that turn many to righteousness, shall shine as the Stars for ever
and ever.

Matthew. 13 43. Then shall the just men shine as the Sun in the Kingdom of
their Father: He that has ears to hear, let him hear, etc.

And as we may comfort our selves by the meditation of these distinct glories
in our bodies then, so it may add unto our comfort, and the establishment of
it, if we consider three things more; to wit, first, the certainty of all
this, that it shall come. Secondly, the shortness of the time thither.
Thirdly, the condition of the body till then.

For the first, we should not doubt of it, because we are borne again to this
hope, we are children of the resurrection now, and so called, Luke 20.36. And
besides, Christ has a charge to loose nothing; no, not of the bodies of the
Saints, Ioh. 6.39. And this is the Fathers will, which has sent me, that of
all which he has given me, I should loose nothing, but should raise it up
again at the last day.

And he came to this end, to dissolve the works of the devil, which is sin,
and death by sin, 1. John. 3.8. Christ also is the first fruit of ye dead, 1.
Cor. 15.20. And further we have felt of the power of Christ in raising our
souls already: he that by his word made all things, can by the same voice
bring back our bodies again.

Ob. That the bodies resolved to dust and ashes, should rise, is against common
sense and reason.

Solut. It is above reason, but not against it. Can men of ashes make glass,
and cannot God of dust make again the body?

Ob. But the bodies dead are often mingled with the bodies of beasts or other
creatures.

Sol. The Goldsmith by his art can sever metals, and extract one metal out
of another, and cannot God distinguish these dusts, etc?

Ob. Flesh and blood cannot come into the Kingdom of heaven. 1. Cor. 15.50.

Sol. By flesh and blood is not meant the body simply, but as it is clothed
with sin and infirmity, which shall be done away in the resurrection.

Ob. The condition of man and beast is one, Eccles. 3.19. For the condition of
the children of men, and the condition of beasts are even as one condition unto
them: As the one dies, so dies the other: for they have all one breath, and
there is no excellency of man above the beast; for all is vanity.

Sol. First, they are like in dying, not in the estate after death. Secondly,
it may be said, those words are the objection of the Epicure, not the opinion
of Solomon.

(...) second, it may add to our comfort, that the Lord is at hand, Phil. 4.5.
and that it is but a little season thither to, Revel. 6.11.

(...) third, the present condition of our bodies even in the grave should
comfort us: for

1. The covenant of God is of force even with them, as they lie in the dust of
the earth, Mat. 22. 31.32.

2. The union with Christ holds still, Col. 1.18.

3. They are not dead, but a sleep in Jesus, 1. These. 4.13.

(...) fourth, woe unto wicked men, even because of the resurrection: they shall
sleep for a while in their bodies, but when they wake, they must be had away to
execution. They that have done evil shall rise unto shame, and contempt, and
condemnation: their bodies shall rise in dishonor, deformity, passible,
tormented with eternal and unutterable tortures, living in darkness without
light, (living, I say for ever, only to feel the pains of eternal dying)
shut up in prison, and denied the comfort of the meanest creatures; it were
well for them, if they did never rise, Revel. 20.14.15. Dan. 12.2. John, 5.29.

CHAP. XXVII. Of the last Judgment.
2. Cor. 5.10. For we must all appear before the judgment seat of Christ,
that every man may receive the things which are done in his body, according to
that he has done, whether it be good or evil.


HItherto of the Resurrection; the last Judgment follows.

The Principles concerning the last judgment are these:

First, that there shall be a general judgment, Jude, 14.15. And Enoch also,
the seventh from Adam, prophesied of such, saying: Behold, the Lord comes
with thousand of Saints:

To give judgment against all men, and to rebuke all the ungodly among them of
all their wicked deeds, which they have ungodly committed, and of all their
cruel speakings, which wicked sinners have spoken against him.

Psalm. 9.8. For he shall judge the world in righteousness, and shall judge
the people with equity.

Psalm. 50.1. The God of Gods, even the Lord has spoken, and called the earth
from the rising up of the Sun, unto the going down thereof, etc.

Heb. 9.27. And as it is appointed unto men, that they shall once die, and after
that comes the judgment.

Dan. 7.9.10. I beheld till the thrones were set up, and the Ancient of days
did sit, whose garment was white as snow, and the hair of his head like the
pure wool: his throne was like the fiery flame, and his wheels as burning
fire:

A fiery stream issued, and came forth from before him: thousand thousands
ministered unto him, and ten thousand thousands stood before him: the Judgment
was set, and the books opened.

Secondly, that Christ shall be the Judge, and that in the humane nature, Act.
10.42. And he commanded us to preach unto the people, and to testify that it
is he, that is ordained of God a Judge of quick and dead.

Acts 17.13. Because he has appointed a day, in the which he will judge the
world in righteousness by that man, whom he has appointed, whereof he has
given an assurance to al men, in that he raised him from the dead.

2. Tim. 4.1. I charge thee therefore before God, and before the Lord Jesus
Christ, which shall judge the quick and dead at his appearing, and in his
Kingdom.

John 5.22. For the Father judges no man, but has committed all judgment
unto the Son.

Ob. The Apostles shall judge the twelve Tribes, Matthew. 19.28.

Sol. 1. The Apostles judge the twelve Tribes by their faith and doctrine, the
example whereof shall take away all excuse from the Israelites.

2. They shall be as Justices of Peace on the Bench, and consent to Christ's
judgment.

Ob. The Saints shall judge the world, 1. Cor. 6.2.

Sol. As assessors with Christ, bearing witness to it, approouing it, and
assenting to it, as the Apostles before.

2. As they are members of Christ the Judge.

3. As their example shall be alleged to condemn the wicked.

Ob. But the Father and holy Ghost judge too.

Sol. The Father does judge by the Son, as by his representative Wisdom,
John 5.22. For the Father judges no man, but has committed all judgment unto
the Son.

Dan. 7.13.14. As I beheld in visions by night, behold, one like the Son of
Man came in the clouds of heaven, and approached unto the Ancient of days, and
they brought him before him;

14. And he gave him dominion, and honor, and a Kingdom, that all people,
nations, etc. Or thus: the authority of judging is common to the three persons,
but the execution only proper to the Son.

Thirdly, all men shall be judged at that day: just and unjust; quick and
dead; small and great, Jude 15. To give judgment against all men, and to
rebuke all the ungodly among them.

Romans 14.9. For Christ therefore died, and rose again, and revived, that he
might be Lord both of the dead, and the quick, etc.

2. Cor. 5.10. For we must all appear before the judgment seat of Jesus
Christ, etc.

To. 14.10. We shall all appear before the judgment seat of Jesus Christ.

Psalm. 9.8. For he shall judge the world.

Object. All men are believers, or unbelievers; now the believers shall not
come unto judgment: as appears, Ioh. 5.24. Verily verily I say unto you, he
that hears my word, and believes in him that sent me, has everlasting life,
and shall not come into condemnation, but has passed from death unto life. And
the unbeliever is condemned already, Ioh. 3.18. He that believes not is
condemned already.

Solution. The believer shall not come into the judgment of condemnation, and
the unbeliever is condemned already in effect and substance: 1. In the counsel
of God: 2. In the word of God: 3. In his own conscience, but yet the
manifestation and finishing of this judgment remains unto the last day.

Fourthly, all the secret things of men's natures, or works shall be brought to
light, Luke 8.17. For nothing is secret, that shall not be evident: neither any
thing hid, that shall not be known, and come to light.

1. Cor. 4.5. Therefore judge nothing before the time, until the Lord come,
who will lighten things that are hid in darkness, and make the counsels of the
heart manifest.

Romans 2.16. At that day God shall judge the secrets of men by Jesus Christ. And
therefore called a day of revelation or declaration, Romans 2.5.

Fifthly, it shall be at the last day, but the precise day and hour is not
known to any men or Angels; the proof for the like principle concerning the
resurrection, serves for this place, Mat. 24.36.

Sixthly, the judgment shall be most just and righteous, and all shall
confess it, Romans 14.10. But why do thou judge thy brother? or why do thou
despise thy brother? for we shall all appear bofore the judgment seat of
Christ.

2. Tim. 4.8. For henceforth is laid up for me the crown of righteousness,
which the Lord the righteous judge shall give me at that day: and not to me
only, but unto all them also which love his appearing, etc.

Romans 2.5. But thou, after thine hardness, and heart that cannot repent, heapest
unto thy self wrath against the day of wrath, and of the declaration of the
just judgment of God.

Psalm. 9.8. For he shall judge the world with righteousness, and shall judge
the people with equity.

Seventhly, the judgment shall be according to men's works, 2. Cor. 5.10.
Every man shall receive the things which are done in his body, according to
that he has done, whether it be good or evil, etc.

Romans 2.6. Who will reward every man according to his works.

Object. We are justified by faith alone without works.

Solution. 1. Works are inquired after in the last judgment, as the signs of
faith, and unbelief.

Sol. 2. We are justified by faith only, but shall be judged by faith and
works both together. For that, judgment does not serve to make men just, that
are unjust, but only to manifest them to be so indeed, which were so in this
life being truly justified.

The consideration whereof should serve for diverse uses, and first for
instruction, and so it should teach us,

First in general, speedily to repent us of our sins, and it should stir
us to all possible care of holy life, and to the love of all well doing, by
which our reckoning might then be furthered, Act. 17.31.

2. Pet. 3.11. Seeing therefore that all these things must be dissolved, what
manner persons ought ye to be in holy conversation and godliness?

14. Wherefore beloved, seeing you look for such things, be diligent, that ye
may be found of him in peace, without spot and blameless.

Philip. 1.10. That ye may discern things that differ one from another, that
ye may be pure and without offense, until the day of Christ.

Tit. 2.12.13. And teaches us that we should deny ungodliness and worldly
lusts and that we should live s^berly, and ^ighteously, and godly in this
present world.

Looking for the blessed hope and appearing of the glory of the mighty God, and
of our Savior Jesus Christ.

Secondly, in particular it should teach us,

1. Not to doat upon earthly things, seeing they must all be consumed in that
day in the fire.

2. To be patient under all wrongs, seeing we are assured there shall be
vengeance rendered at that day, 2. These. 1.5.6.7. Iam. 5.6.7. Phil. 4.5.

Thirdly, to take heed of rashness in judging other men: and men offend in
censuring;

1. When they inflict censures, and meddle over busily, or curiously with them
that be without, 1. Cor. 5.12. For what have I to do, to judge them which are
without?

2. When men speak evil of that which is good, and call good evil, Esa.
5.20. Woe unto them that speak good of evil, and evil of good; which put
darkness for light, and light for darkness; that put bitter for sweet, and sweet
for sour.

3. When men judge of things doubtful, as the hidden things of the heart, and
the secret things of darkness, 1. Cor. 4.5. Therefore judge nothing before the
time, until the Lord come, who will lighte^ things that are hid in darkness, and
make the counsels of the heart manifest. And censure things in the worst sense.

4. When men uncharitably censure others about things indifferent, Romans 14.3.4.
Let not him that eats, despise him that eats not; and let not him which
eats not, judge him that eats, for God has received him.

4. Who art thou that condemnest another man's servant? he stands or falls
to his own master: yea he shall be established; for God is able to make him
stand, etc.

13. Let us not therefore judge one another any more, but use your judgment
rather in this, that no man put an occasion to fall, or a stumbling block
before his brother.

5. When men commit, what they condemn, Romans 2.1.2. Therefore thou art
inexcusable, O man, whosoever thou art that iudgest? for in that thou iudgest
another, thou condemnest thy self; for thou that iudgest, do the same things.

But we know, that the judgment of God is according to truth, against them
which commit such things. Or being guilty of greater faults, condemn others
for lesser, Mat. 7.1.2.3. Judge not, that ye be not judged.

And why see thou the mote that is in thy brothers eye, and perceiuest not
the beam, that is in thine own eye, etc.

6. When men make a fault worse then it is.

Fourthly, it should strike a fear into our hearts concerning God, and his
dreadful Majesty, and Justice; and make us afraid to offend him, and seek by
all means to glorify him, whatsoever become of us and the world, Revel. 14.7.
Saying with a loud voice; fear God, and give glory to him; for the hour of
his judgment is come; and worship him that made heaven and earth, and the sea,
and the fountain of waters, etc.

Fifthly, we should be sober, in not enquiring into things not revealed, and
look to the maine business: as for the precise time, or place of the
judgment, or from whence the fire shall come that shall burn all, or what
kind kind of throne it shall be, or what the sign of the Son of man shall be,
or such like; we believe that they shall be, but ought not to enquire when,
where, or how they shall be.

Sixthly, chiefly this doctrine of the last judgment should compel in all of
us a care so to live, that we may be sure to have comfort in that day: and that
we shall be sure to find;

1. If we believe in Jesus Christ, Ioh. 5.24. Verily verily I say unto you,
he that hears my word, and believes in him that sent me, has everlasting
life, and shall not come into condemnation, but has passed from death unto
life.

2. If we be sure to judge our selves here, God will not condemn us with the
world, 1. Cor. 11.31. For if we would judge our selves, we should not be
judged, etc.

3. If continually we consult with the word of God, to see that our deeds be
wrought in God, Ioh. 3.19.20.21. He that does truth, comes to the light,
that his deeds might be made manifest, that they are wrought according to God.

4. If we watch and pray always, they that pray much on earth, shall stand
before Christ with comfort at that day, Luke 21.36. Watch therefore and pray
continually, that ye may be counted worthy to escape all these things that
shall come to pass, and that ye may stand before the Son of man.

5. If we be merciful and loving, and bountiful to the godly in their
distresses, Matthew. 25. 31 etc.

6. If we be sheep; sheep I say: 1. For tractablenesse, so as we know,
hear, and be ruled by the voice of Christ. 2. For sociablenesse: a sheep will
not be alone, nor sort with swine. 3. For profitablenesse* that we be not
idle, nor unfruitful, Mat. 25. Ioh. 10.

7. If we can get the seal of the spirit, as our earnest of our final
redemption at that day; the witness of the spirit in this life will make all
sure against that day, Ephesians. 1.14. The spirit of promise is the earnest of our
inheritance, until the redemption of the possession purchased unto the praise
of his glory.

Romans 8.15. For ye have not received the spirit of bondage to fear again, but
ye have received the spirit of adoption, whereby we cry Abba Father.

8. If we hold fast what we have, and loose not what we have wrought, Revel.
3.11. Behold I come shortly; hold that which thou have, that no man take thy
crown.

2. Ioh. 8. Look to your selves, that we loose not the things which we have
done, but that we may receive a full reward.

9. If we often receive the Sacrament of the Lords Supper with due
preparation: for therein

1. Christ does familiarly converse with us, and is given to our nourishment to
eternal life.

2. The outward elements are unfeigned pledges of the remission of all our
sins.

3. We therein remember the death of Christ for us, and how he was judged for
our sakes, and thereby have our hearts settled against the fear of any severity
from him.

4. In the right preparation for the Sacrament, we prepare for the last
judgment too; one work serves to both purposes.

5. The Sacraments are Gods broad seals, to assure us that we shall speed well
at that day.

Thus of the uses for instruction.

Secondly, this doctrine of the last judgment has singular terror in it to
all impenitent sinners, which may be considered either more generally, or more
particularly.

First, in general, it is terrible for them to hear, and know, that God has
set them a day, and has given them final warning to repent; or else
undoubtedly he will judge them with all severity, Act. 17.31. Because he has
appointed a day, in the which he will judge the world in righteousness, by
that man whom he has appointed, whereof he has given an assurance unto all
men, in that he has raised him from the dead.

Jude 15. To give judgment against all men, and to rebuke all the ungodly
among them of all their wicked deeds, which they have ungodly committed, and of
all their cruel speaking, which wicked sinners have spoken against him.

Romans 2.5. But thou after thine hardness, and heart that cannot repent,
heapest unto thy self wrath against the day of wrath, and of the declaration
of the just judgment of God.

Who will reward every man according to his works, etc.

Secondly, in particular, this terror is the more grievous, if they consider
either the distinct miseries shall then fall upon the^, or the several sins
God has reserved to trial and punishment at that day.

What heart ca^ stand before the serious thoughts of ye particulars?

1. They shall hear the thunder of Christ's fearful voice summoning them.

2. They shall be chased in by the Angels before Christ, from all the four
winds of heaven.

3. They shall be set at Christ's lefthand, as a sign of miserable disgrace,
Matthew. 25.33.

4. A fire shall devour before Christ, and it shall be tempestuous round about
him, Psalm. 50.3. Our God shall come, and shall not keep silence; a fire shall
devour before him, and a mighty tempest shall be moved round about him, etc.

2. These. 1.8. In flaming fire rendering vengeance unto them, that do not know
God, and which obey not unto the Gospel of our Lord Jesus Christ.

5. They shall be everlastingly shamed, and before all the world, Dan. 12.2. And
many of them, that sleep in the dust of the earth shall awake, some to
everlasting life, and some to shame and perpetual contempt; when all their
sins shall be discovered, and set in order before them, Psalm. 50.21. These
things have thou done, and I held my tongue; therefore thou thoughtst, that I
was like thee: but I will reprove thee, and set them in order before thee, etc.

6. They shall be sentenced to eternal condemnation, containing in it,

1. Separation from God, Christ, and all the godly, Go ye cursed, etc. Matthew.
25.41. etc.

2. Pain and anguish unutterable, Romans 2.9. Tribulation and anguish shall be
upon the soul of every man that does evil: of the Jew first, and also of the
Grecian.

3. Fellowship with the Devil and his Angels, Matthew. 25. 41. as a little
before.

Ob. Some one might say, We hope it is not certain, that there shall be such a
day.

Sol. It is most certain, It is appointed, as certain, as that men shall die,
Heb. 9.27. And as it is appointed unto men, that they shall once die, and after
that comes the judgment.

Acts 17.31. Because he has appointed a day, in the which he will judge the
world in righteousness, etc.

Besides, the terrible plagues, which have been and are in the world, shows,
that God is extremely wrath with sin, and will call to judgment; such as the
drowning of the old world, burning of Sodom, swallowing up of Corath, Dathan,
and Abiram; the neglect of the Gentiles, the reiection of the Jews, the
punishing of Christ, the afflictions of the godly, the wars, pestilences,
famins, etc. that are in the world.

And they themselves may guess somewhat at it, by the sharpenes of the word,
the accusing of the conscience, the checkes of the spirit, and the fearful
terrors of conscience which fall upon some men.

Ob. But God we hope will be merciful.

Sol. It is a day of wrath, not of mercy; the date of mercy will be then out,
Romans 2.5. But thou after thine hardness and heart, which cannot repent,
heapest unto thy self wrath against the day of wrath, and of the declaration
of the just judgment of God, etc.

Ob. But God says nothing to me all this while: I escape, and am not troubled;
I discern no way that God is displeased with me.

Sol. 1. Seaes of wrath hang over thy head daily, though thou discern them
not, John 3. vlt. He that believes in the Son has everlasting life, and he
that obeys not the Son, shall not see the life, but the wrath of God
abides on him.

Sol. 2. Many signs of Gods displeasure are upon thy soul, though thou feel
them not. It is one extreme curse to be left off unto such a spirit of slumber.

3. Though God does not yet discover to thee his displeasure, yet will he
awake to thy judgment, Psalm. 50.31. These things have thou done, and I held
my tongue; therefore thou thoughtst, that I was like thee: but I will reprove
thee, and set them in order before thee.

Ob. But I may find some means to help my self at that day.

Sol. Riches will not avail in the day of wrath, Job, 36.18. For Gods wrath
is, lest he should take thee away in thine abundance: for no multitude of gifts
can deliver thee.

Verse. 19. Will he regard thy riches? he regards not gold, nor all them that
excel in strength. And there shall be none to deliver, Psalm. 50.22. O
consider this, ye that forget God; lest I tear you in pieces, and there be
none that can deliver you, etc.

Ob. But I may then repent.

Sol. No: As death leaves thee, so shall judgment find thee; it is a day of
the declaration of the righteous judgment of God, Romans 2.5. But thou after
thine hardness, and heart, that cannot repent, heapest unto thy self wrath
against the day of wrath, and of the declaration of the just judgment of God.

2. Cor. 5.10. For we must all appear before the judgment seat of Christ,
that every man receive the things which are done in his body, according to
that he has done, whether it be good or evil.

Ob. But there is a world of people in the same case.

Sol. He will judge all the ungodly, he cares not for the multitude, Jude, 15.
To give judgment against all men, and to rebuke all the ungodly amongst them
of all their wicked deeds, which they have ungodly committed, and of al their
cruel speaking, which wicked sinners have spoken against him.

Besides, he has plagued multitudes, as the old World, etc. and he can easily
do execution: for he comes with thousand thousands of his Angels, Jude, 14.
And Enoch also, the seventh from Adam, prophesied of such, saying, Behold, the
Lord comes with thousands of his Saints.

Ob. But who knows my faults?

Sol. 'The hidden things of darkness, and the secrets of men's hearts shall then
be discovered, 1. Cor. 4.5. Therefore judge nothing before the time until the
Lord come, who will lighten things, that are hid in darkness, and make the
counsels of the hearts manifest, and then shall every man have praise of God.

Ob. But by what evidence can I be convinced? God may forget my faults before
then.

Sol. No: God has them written in his book of remembrance with a pen of iron,
and a point of a diamond, Ier. 17.1. The sin of Judah is written with a pen of
iron, and with the point of a diamond, and graven upon the table of your
hearts, and upon the horns of your altars. And evidence will be easy to be
had upon the opening of these books, Revel* 20.12. And I saw the dead both
great and small stand before God, and the books were opened: and another book
was opened, which is the book of life, and the dead were judged of those
things which are written in the books, according to their works.

Besides, the Heavens will declare his righteousness, Psalm. 50.6. And the
creatures abused by them, will give in evidence against them, Ier. 17.1. And
the word that men have heard shall judge them. And their own consciences shall
be dilated, and be in stead of a thousand witnesses: and the Spirit of God
that has so often reproved the world of sin, can easily accuse them, Ioh.
16.8. And when he is come, he will reprove the world of sin, and of
righteousness, and of judgment, etc.

Ob. I know no great fault by my self.

Sol. Though thou forget thy sins; yet Christ will remember them, Matthew. 25.
It will not serve the turn to say, When did we so?

Ob. But I never did Christ any great wrong.

Sol. Thou have many ways sinned against Christ, though thy careless heart
perceive it not: but if thou had not, yet in as much as thou have done wrong
to Christians, thou have done it to Christ, Matthew. 25.

Ob. But I have done much good in the world.

Sol. If thou have not had true faith, and love, and repentance, it shall not
avail thee, as these places show, 1. Cor. 13.3. And though I feed the poor
with all my goods, and though I give my body, that I be burned, and have not
love, it profits me nothing.

Ob. But we never had such means of knowledge, as others have had.

Sol. They that have sinned without the Law, shall be judged without the Law;
and they that have sinned under the Law, shall be judged by the Law, Romans 2.
12. For as many as have sinned without the Law, shall perish also without the
law; and as many as have sinned in the Law, shall be judged by the Law.

Ob. But it is a great while thither.

Sol. It is not: for the Lord is at hand, 1. Pet. 4.7. Now the end of all
things is at hand; be you therefore sober, and watching in prayer.

Iam. 5.8. Be ye also patient therefore, and settle your hearts; for the coming
of the Lord draws near.

Besides, the signs of the last judgment are the most of them accomplished
already; Antichrist is revealed, and almost pulled down, 2. Thessalon. 2. 1.
John 2.18. The World has been full of spirits of deceivers, 1. Tim. 4.1. The
sins of the last age are every where at the full: Iniquity abounds, 2.
Timoth. 3.1. Matthew. 24.12. The powers of heaven are shaken, which appears by
the often Eclipses of Sun and Moon; and by the uncertainty of the Seasons
both in Summer and Winter, Matthew. 24.29. The sea roares and is outrageous; men
are secure now as in the days of Noah, Matthew. 24.37.

3. Were it that it were further off: yet the day of death, which is the day of
thy particular judgment, is not far off.

Ob. But yet sure there will be some kind of warning.

Sol. No: he will come suddenly, as the thief in the night, 1. These. 5.2.3.
For ye your selves know perfectly, that the day of the Lord shall come, eue^ as
a thief in the night.

For when they shall say, peace and safety, then shall come upon them sudden
destruction, as the travail upon a woman with child, and they shall not
escape.

Mat. 24.39. And knew nothing, till the flood came, and took them all away; so
shall also the coming of the Son of Man be,

And the rather should men be affected with the terror of this day, and be
thereby persuaded to repentance:

1. Because God will be Judge himself, Psalm. 50.6. and therefore there can be
no appeal, he being supreme Judge.

2. Because it is a final sentence, there will be no time of respit, or
change, or reuocation.

3. Because they shall be judged by him, whom they have so much despised, and
wronged, Revel. 1.7.8. Behold, he comes in the clouds, and every eye shall
see him; yea, even they which pierced him through, and all kindreds of the
earth shall wail before him.

4. Because Gods proceedings shall be all cleared, and every tongue shall
confess, that God has done nothing but Justice, Romans 2.5. It is a day of the
declaration of the just judgment of God: and Romans 14.11.

And this justice will the more appear

1. By the equity of Gods dealing: they have had their days of sin, and
therefore reason he should have his day of wrath, Romans 2.5.

2. By the consideration of his patience, what a wonderful while has God
deferred this last judgment, 2. Pet. 3.9. The Lord is not slack concerning his
promise, as some men count slacknesse, but is patient toward us, and would have
no man to perish, but would all men to come to repentance.

Romans 2.4. Or despisest thou the riches of his bountifulness, and patience,
and long suffering, not knowing that the bountifulness of God leads thee to
repentance, etc.

3. God will then discover a world of offenses in every wicked man, that are
not now known.

4. God will then unfold the secrets of his Counsel, and bring forth exquisite
reasons of his proceedings, which are now like a great deep unto us, Romans
11.33. O the deepenesse of the riches, both of the wisdom, and knowledge of
God! how unsearchable are his judgments, and his ways past finding out! etc.

And as this doctrine is terrible, in respect of the parts of their misery,
and in respect of the taking off of all objections: so is it, because the
particular sinners are particularly mentioned in Scripture, that shall be sure
to speed ill at that day: for Christ with terror will then judge,

1. The man of sin, who shall be sure to be consumed with the breath of his
mouth, though he lord it for a time over all that is called God, 2. These. 2.4.

2. All that worship the beast, and receive his mark, shall be cast into the
lake that burns with fire and brimstone, Revel. 19.20. and 14.9.10.

3. All Atheistical mockers of religion, and the coming of Christ, 2. Pet.
3.3.

4. All false teachers, which bring in damnable heresies, 2. Pet. 2.1.

5. All Apostates, that sin willingly after they have received the truth, Hebr.
10.26. For if we sin willingly after that we have received the knowledge of
the truth, there remains no more sacrifice for sins.

27. But a fearful looking for of judgment, and violent fire, which shall
devour the adversaries, etc.

6. All goats, that is, unruly Christians, that will not be kept within the
mou^ds of Christ's government, Matthew. 25.32.

7. All Hypocrites shall then be unmasked, Luke 12.1.2. Psalm. 50.17. Take heed
to your selves of the leven of the Pharisees, which is hypocrisy.

2. For there is nothing covered, that shall not be revealed, neither hid,
that shall not be known.

8. All railers shall receive the punishment of their ungodly words, Psalm.
50.19. Jude 15. To give judgment against all men, and to rebuke all the
ungodly among the^ of all their wicked deeds, which they have ungodly
committed, and of all their cruel speaking, which wicked sinners have spoken
against him, etc.

9. All censorious and masterlike men, that judge other men in what they are
guilty themselves, Romans 2.1. Therefore thou art inexcusable, O man, whosoever
thou art, that iudgest: for in that that thou iudgest another, thou condemnest
thy self, for thou that iudgest do the same things.

3. And think thou this, O thou man, that iudgest them which do such
things, and do the same, that thou shall escape the judgment of God, etc?

Iam. 3.1. etc. My brethren, be not many masters, knowing that we shall
receive the greater condemnation, etc.

10. All merciless and covetous rich men, Iam. 5.1. Go to now ye rich men,
weep, and howl for your miseries, that shall come upon you.

2. Your riches are corrupt, and your garments are moth-eaten.

3. Your gold and silver is cankred, and the rust of them shall be a witness
against you, and shall eat your flesh as it were fire, ye have heaped up
treasures for the last days.

5. Ye have lived in pleasure on the earth, and in wantonness; ye have
nourished your hearts as in a day of slaughter.

Matthew. 25.41. Then shall he say unto them on the left hand, depart from me ye
cursed into everlasting fire, which is prepared for the devil and his angels.

42. For I was an hungered, and you gave me no meat; I thirsted, and ye gave me
no drink, etc.

Iam. 2.13. For there shall be judgment merciless, to him that shows no
mercy.

11. All whoremongers and adulterers, Heb. 13.4. Marriage is honorable among
all, and the bed undefiled: but whoremongers and adulterers God will judge, etc.

12. All drunkards and Epicures, Luke 21.34. Take heed to your selves, lest at
any time your hearts be oppressed with surfeiting and drunkenness, and cares
of this life, and lest that day come upon you at unawares.

13. All deceitful persons with their scant measures, and false waights, Mich.
6.10.11. Are yet the treasures of wickedness in the house of the wicked, and
the scant measure that is abominable?

Shall I justify the wicked balances, and the bag of deceitful waights?

14. All liars, and all that love lies, Revel. 21.8. But the fearful, and
unbelieving, and the abominable, and murderers, and whoremongers, and
sorcerers, and idolaters, and all liars, shall have their part in the lake
which burns with fire and brimstone, which is the second death.

Revel. 22.15. For without shall be dogs, and enchanters, and whoremongers and
murderers, and idolaters, and whosoever loves, or makes lies, etc.

15. Lastly, all that disobey the Gospel, 2. These. 1.8. In flaming fire,
rendering vengeance unto them that do not know God, and which obey not unto the
Gospel of our Lord Jesus Christ.

And thus for terror.

Lastly, the doctrine of the last judgment should be exceeding comfortable to
all the godly, and that in many respects:

First, if they shall consider who shall be their Judge, even he that is their
brother, husband, advocate, head, and redeemer: he that was judged for their
sakes; and therefore they need to fear no hard sentence from him.

Secondly, if they consider the present assurance of hope.

For first, has not Christ given them many promises, that it shall go well
with them at that day?

2. Has not Christ justified them already, and absolved the^ from all their
sins? Romans 3.24.25.

3. Have they not received the earnest of the spirit, and the seal of the
Sacraments? 2. Cor. 1.21.22. 2. Cor. 5.5.

4. Have they not judged themselves, and therefore are they not free from
condemnation with the world? 1. Cor. 11.31.32.

5. They have been judged already, the afflictions of this life will be
accounted sufficient unto them, 1. Pet. 4.17.

They may trust their souls to God: and that God, that has begun his good
work in them, will perform it till the day of Christ, Philip. 1.5.6. 1. Cor.
1.8.

Thirdly, if they consider the benefits they shall attain unto at that day:
for Christ will be made marvelous in all them that believe, 2. These. 1.10.
They shall have honor, and praise; their innocence shall be cleared, and their
miseries and sins ended. And when Christ shall appear, then shall we also
appear with him in glory, Colos. 3.4.

Fourthly, if they consider the circumstances of the Judgment, as

1. The neernesse of the time should make them hold up their heads, Matthew.
24.22.33.

Philip. 4.5. Let your patient mind be known unto all men, the Lord is at hand.

Iam. 5.8. Be ye also patient therefore, and settle your hearts for the coming
of the Lord draws near.

2. The greatness of the assembly, before whom they shall be so much graced
by Christ, they shall be honored before all men, and Angels.

3. The condition of the sentence, it shall be a final sentence never to be
revoked, but acknowledged to all eternity.

4. And besides, they shall have this favor, that nothing shall be remembered
but goodness in good men: their sins shall not be mentioned unto them,
Matthew. 25.

CHAP. XXVIII. Of the glory of heaven.
1. Cor. 2.9. But as it is written, The things which eye has not seen,
neither ear has heard, neither came into man's heart, are, which God has
prepared for them that love him.


HItherto of the principles that concern the resurrection, and the last
judgment: The principles that concern the glory of heaven follow.

There are four principles concerning the glory of heaven.

The first concerns the greatness of it: It is unspeakable, and in respect of
us here on earth, incomprehensible, 1. Cor. 2.9. as in the beginning.

1. Ioh. 3.2. Dearly beloved, now are we the sons of God, but yet it does not
appear what we shall be, and we know, that when we shall appear, we shall be
like him; for we shall see him as he is.

Colos. 3.3.4. For ye are dead, and your life is hid with Christ in God.

When Christ which is our life shall appear, then shall we also appear with
him in glory.

2. Cor. 12.4. How that he was taken up into Paradise, and heard words which
cannot be spoken, which are not possible for man to utter,

Revel. 2.17. Let him that has an ear hear, what the spirit says unto the
Churches: to him that overcomes will I give to eat of the manna that is hid,
and will give him a white stone, and in the stone a new name written, which no
man knows saving he that receives it.

Psalm. 16.11. Thou will show me the path of life, in thy presence is the
fullness of joy, and at thy right hand there are pleasures for evermore.

Psalm. 31.19. How great is thy goodness, which thou have laid up for them
that fear thee, and done to them that trust in thee, even before the sons of
men?

The second concerns the continuance of it, and so it is eternal; and
therefore is this life called eternal life, and immortality, Matthew 25. verse.
46. And these shall go into everlasting pain, and the righteous into life
eternal.

2. Timoth. 1.10. But is now made manifest by the appearing of our Savior
Jesus Christ, who has abolished death, and has brought life and immortality
unto light, through the Gospel.

1. Pet. 1.4. To an inheritance immortal, and undefiled, and that fades not
away, reserved in heaven for you, etc.

2. Cor. 5.1. For we know, that if our earthly house of this tabernacle be
destroyed, we have a building given of God, that is, an house not made with
hands, but eternal in the heavens.

The third concerns the cause of it: Heaven is the gift of God, and proceeds
only from his free grace, and not for any merit in us, Luke 12.32. Fear not
little flock, for it is your Fathers pleasure to give you a kingdom.

Titus 3.4. But when the bountifulness and love of God our Savior toward man
appeared; not for our righteousness, but according to his mercy he saved us,
etc.

Ioh. 3.16. For God so loved the world, that he has given his only begotten
Son, that whosoever believes in him should not perish, but have everlasting
life.

Romans 6.23. For the wages of sin is death; but the gift of God is eternal
life, through Jesus Christ our Lord, etc.

1. Pet. 1. all the chapter.

The fourth concerns the persons that shall enjoy it: the elect of God only
obtain this glory, 1. Cor. 15.50. etc. This say I brethren, that flesh and
blood cannot inherit the kingdom of God, neither does corruption inherit
incorruption.

Revel. 21.27. And there shall enter into it none unclean thing, neither
whatsoever works abomination, or lies, but they which are written in the
Lambs book of life.

1. Cor. 6.9. Know ye not that the unrighteous shall not inherit the kingdom
of God? be not deceived: Neither fornicators, nor Idolaters, nor adulterers,
nor wantons, nor buggeres, etc.

Romans 2.7. That is to them which by continuance in well doing, seek glory, and
honor, and immortality, eternal life.

10. But to every man that does good, shall be glory, and honor, and peace, to
the Jew first, and also to the Grecian.

The uses follow, and are either for instruction, or for consolation.

First, for instruction: and then the doctrine of the glory of heaven should
work diverse impressions upon our hearts.

1. We should with all earnestness importune God, to enable us to behold by
the effectualnesse of contemplation, the greatness of that felicity, is
provided for us in heaven: we are naturally extremely unable for the
contemplation of it, we should beseech God by his spirit to force open our
eyes, and make us able to stand and gaze with admiration at the glory to come,
Ephesians. 1.18.19. Romans 5.2.3.

2. Our hearts should be fiered with an ardency of desire, and endeavor to
praise the glorious and free grace of God, which has without our deserts
appointed us unto such glory; we can never walk worthy of heaven, till we be
fitted to a daily and affectionate praise of Gods love to us therein: All ages
should stand and wonder at such rich grace and tender kindness of God in Jesus
Christ, Ephesians. 1.6. Ephesians. 2.7.

Thirdly, it should raise up in us a wonderful estimation of the godly, who
are therefore the only excellent Ones, because as princes of God they are borne
heirs to so great a Kingdom: No meanness of their outward condition should
abate of our reverence to them, that are so rich in faith, and heirs of such
glory, etc. Psalm. 6.3. James 2.5.

And seeing we must live with them for ever, we should choose them, as the most
happy companions of our lives here, and receive them, as Christ received us to
glory, Romans 15.7. 1. Ioh. 4.7.17, etc. And live in all peace with them, Ephesians.
4.23. And for this reason husbands should make much of their godly wives, as
heirs with them of the same grace of God, 1. Peter 3.8. And Masters should use
with all respect their religious servants, knowing that of the Lord, their
very servants shall receive the reward of inheritance, Colos. 3.23.24.

Fourthly, it should exceedingly raise the price of godliness, and make us with
all hearty affection deuote our selves to weldoing, seeing there is such an
invaluable gain arises unto such, as with patience and painfulness continue
in doing good: we should be abundant in the work of the Lord; if for no
reason, yet because of the great reward in heaven, 1. Cor. 15.58. Romans 2.7.10.

Fifthly, it should make us to take off our affections from the World, with
disdain and indignation at our selves for being so foolish, as to settle our
hearts on things below. And since necessity enioynes us to use the world, this
religious hope should make us use it, as if we used it not, expressing all
sobriety and temperance, and contempt of those transitory things, and setting
our hearts there, where those matchless treasures are. What profit is it to
win all this World, if our souls be shut out of Heaven? and what loss can it
be, if we loose this World, and find our right unto the World to come? This
doctrine should make us feelingly know, and profess our selves to be
strangers and pilgrims here; and to desire to be no other, then such, as long
to be absent from hence, that we may be present with the Lord in this glory.

1. Cor. 7.31. Col. 3.1.2. 1. Pet. 1.13. Matthew. 6.19.20. Matthew 16.25.26. Heb.
11.13. 2. Cor. 5.6.

Sixthly, we should be especially careful to be all that, that is required
unto eternal life.

And so in general we must be sure, we be borne again, else Christ is
peremptory, we cannot enter into the Kingdom of heaven, Ioh. 3.5. Heaven is
an inheritance, and therefore we must first be sons. That glory must
penetrate into our hearts by the beams of it, so as we be changed from glory
to glory, 2. Corint. 3.18. We must enter into the first degree of eternal
life, and that is in this life, we must bear the image of Christ.

And in particular, we must distinctly look to these things:

1. We must be careful to be provided of the means to teach us the way to
heaven; we must labor for the meat, that endures to eternal life, John 6.27.
As knowing, that the preaching of the Gospel is the power of God to salvation,
Romans 1.16. Romans 10.14.

2. We must seriously study the mysteries of this Kingdom, and keep our
selves close to profitable things, which may edify us, Matthew. 13.11. Titus
3.8.9.

3. We must purge our selves as he is pure, we must seriously, and soundly
employ our selves in the duties of mortification of our corruptions, 1. John
3.3. And every man tha^ has this hope in him, purges himself, as he is
pure, etc.

4. We must be sure, that the tempter deceive us not in our faith: for that is
our evidence for those things, which are not seen, and that makes them (as it
were) present, Heb. 11.1. Now faith is the ground of things which are hoped
for, and the evidence of things which are not seen.

1. These. 3.5. Even for this cause, when I could no longer forbear, I sent him
that I might know of your faith; lest the tempter had tempted you in any sort,
and that our labor had been in vain.

1 Pet. 1.7. That the trial of your faith, being much more precious then gold
that perishes, though it be tried with fire, might be found unto your praise,
and honor, and glory, at the appearing of Jesus Christ.

2. Cor. 13.5. Prove your selves, whether you are in the faith: examine your
selves, know ye not your own selves, how that Jesus Christ is in you, except
you be reprobates?

For by faith Christ lives in us, Gal. 2.20.

5. We must be sure, we be not ashamed of Christ in this World, and that we
do not deny him here on earth, but contrariwise, Matthew. 10.32. Whosoever
therefore shall confess me before men, him will I confess also before my
Father, which is in heaven.

Verse. 33. But whosoever shall deny me before men, him will I also deny before
